The Daily News stated that the only reliable thing is to consolidate the peace formed by the entire mechanism of the League of Nations. The Evening News requested that Britain should unreservedly participate in group actions to resist any country that attempts to change the map of Europe by force. The Morning Post stated that if anything can make Germany feel that it has fallen into a self-imposed state of isolation and despair, it is Britain's willingness to take the lead. We must abandon fruitless bickering and resolutely participate in safeguarding peace with the only method that can ensure success. The Daily Sketch stated that if Britain refuses to join the disputes in Europe and maintains peace for its own people, it will be respected by everyone. The Daily Mail called for no deals with Russia, no encirclement of Germany, and immediate construction of the strongest air force. (Reuters, 9th)

Broad Security Plan: Does Not Want to Exclude Germany

(London) Parliament predicts that the Cabinet plans to submit to the Stressa Conference a broad plan for mutual air assistance, as Britain's contribution to the security system. This plan is based on limiting the air force strength of various countries. The scope of the so-called security system must be broader than the Eastern European regional pact. Although Britain's attitude to be adopted at the Stressa Conference regarding this matter is currently uncertain, the so-called broad plan may aim to encompass all countries that have participated in the war, without excluding any one. A question arises here, that is, if Germany excludes itself, what will other countries do? The general impression is that if Germany can join this plan, Britain is prepared to recognize its full equality of military rights in exchange. However, the Stressa Conference may not make any decisions regarding this matter before a conference is held by all relevant countries. (Havas, 9th)

Italian-French Solidarity: Difficulties Will Eventually Be Overcome

Soviet Prominent Political Commentator: Reviews Pan-European Convention

(Moscow) Soviet prominent political commentator Radek has an article published in Izvestia, in which Radek stated that the daily news received regarding the preparations for Stressa proves that its future is extremely pessimistic. Radek mentioned the recent rounds of negotiations, saying, "Politics should be based on information, but we can only examine the situation and inform each other until a new world war breaks out. The issue of Eastern European security is primarily related to the Eastern European countries. Since the Stressa Conference does not have their participation, the convention cannot be stipulated by the conference. Considering the Soviet Union's relationship to this issue, a certain decision must be effective only with its participation. The news that has been circulating recently among the great powers regarding the Eastern European regional mutual assistance convention is really confusing. According to some British and French newspapers, a reliable French opinion believes that since Germany and Poland are unwilling to sign this convention, the Eastern Convention will be abandoned and replaced by a pan-European convention. This convention is directly based on the League of Nations Covenant, but it needs to be made more specific."

Radek further reviewed the pan-European convention plan, saying, "Fifteen years of experience have proven that countries have no power to take on a responsibility to provide assistance to an unknown country in an unknown situation and an unknown event without prior knowledge. Has the difficulty encountered by the Eastern Convention changed this experience? If a regional convention is not easy to achieve, then it will be even less likely to realize a system in which all countries take on certain obligations in the event of war. This has been proven by experience. The claim by Poland and Germany that they are unwilling to agree to the Eastern Convention is not convincing, because Germany and Poland cannot bear any definite obligations to several countries with obvious and clear contradictions, and they claim that they can take action against aggressor countries in distant territories and in unknown events? Those who draft this universal convention plan, which includes all countries, aim to keep the Eastern Convention in useless international negotiations for a long time, and that is why the German press supports this plan, but this is not only related to the issue of Germany and Poland. A universal convention that seeks to strengthen the obligations undertaken by various countries is absolutely impossible without Britain's signature. However, Britain is absolutely unwilling to take on more obligations on the continent. If someone requires the British government to be clearly responsible for providing assistance to European countries that are being invaded, they will definitely refuse. At the same time, if their obligations are not clearly stipulated, then they will be of little help in increasing security. On the contrary, this kind of vague obligation can have harmful results, because countries threatened by danger will be softened, thereby helping the aggressor countries complete their goals. Therefore, this universal agreement cannot be accepted. I predict that after several months of diplomatic negotiations, the drafters of this plan will find themselves in the same position and encountering the same difficulties as they are today. The only difference is that those who are willing to start a war have had more time to prepare." (TASS, 8th)

France Intensifies Air Defense: Promulgates New Regulations; All Organizations; Tank Regiment Transferred to Consolidate the Eastern Border 68

(Paris) Today's French government gazette published a new law stipulating the organization of national air defense. In addition to the annual budget, there is a special fund for air defense. The law stipulates that all air defense organizations will be under the jurisdiction of the military authorities in emergencies. Shelters will be added everywhere, and existing buildings must have gas protection equipment. Volunteers who are not in military service, whether male or female, should be conscripted in the event of war. Increase alarm bells to warn the public and expand the fire brigade, etc. The expenses are borne by the government, and each city must also bear one-tenth of the total expenses. Various equipment must be inspected on a regular basis. Those who do not comply with the inspection will be fined 16 to 110 francs for the first time, and if they commit the offense again, they will be fined 200 francs, or imprisoned for one month. The overseas territories will also be the same. (Guomin, 9th)

(Paris) France's 51st Tank Regiment has been stationed in the central town of Bouchis since the European War. It has now been ordered to transfer to the important city of Verdun in order to consolidate the eastern border defense. (Guomin, 9th)

Danzig Election Not Prosperous: The National Socialist Party Did Not Achieve Its Ambitions; The Free City System Cannot Be Changed; Looked at the Victory of the Saar with Disappointment 71

Warsaw: The temporary results of the Danzig City Council election, the distribution of seats is roughly as follows:

National Socialist Party: 43 seats, Social Democratic Party: 12 seats

Catholic Center Party: 10 seats, Communist Party: 2 seats

German National People's Party: 3 seats, Polish Party: 2 seats, totaling 72 seats in the City Council. The National Socialist Party won 43 seats, while the opposition party won 29 seats. (Havas, 8th)

(Berlin) The National Socialist Party is quite disappointed with the results of the Danzig City Council election. The National Socialist Party originally hoped to win at least two-thirds of the seats, so that the opposition party would not be able to do anything, and the system of the Free City of Danzig could be changed at will. In view of the special circumstances of Danzig and the relationship between Germany and Poland, Germany must abide by the procedures stipulated in the Danzig constitution and should not occupy Danzig by force. If the National Socialist Party had won two-thirds of the seats, it could have declared Danzig's merger with Germany in accordance with legal procedures, rendering the provisions of the Treaty of Versailles regarding the Free City of Danzig practically invalid. However, although the National Socialist Party has won six more seats than before in this election, it is still four seats short of the two-thirds majority. Therefore, German newspapers only stated that the number of votes won by the National Socialist Party in Danzig has greatly increased, and did not celebrate the victory of this election. This is quite noteworthy, because some people in the National Socialist Party generally believe that the significance of this election transcends the scope of the city of Danzig. If a great victory had been achieved in Danzig, a precedent would have been set for holding referendums in Memel and even in Austria. But this is not the case now. The election in Danzig failed to achieve its goals, so it is appropriate that the National Socialist Party is greatly disappointed. (Havas, 8th)

(Berlin) The political result of the election in Danzig at present is that the National Socialist Party failed to obtain a two-thirds majority, so it failed to amend the constitution of the Free City, and the opposition party can prevent the National Socialist Party's plan to establish a dictatorship. However, people generally do not believe that the prestige of the National Socialist Party and the people's welcome to the party have declined in Germany proper, because the economic situation of Danzig is far less prosperous than that of Germany, and the local National Socialist Party organs are deeply criticized by the opposition party for their favoritism. Although, the National Socialist Party leaders tried their best to win, but to no avail. Compared with the victory in the Saar region, it is even more disappointing. This is still the first time in the history of the National Socialist Party. (Guomin, 8th)

This is a reiterated statement of reservation by Japan, but it is still unknown whether the League of Nations Council will accept it without criticism. (Reuters, 9th)

After the Belgian Currency Devaluation: The Economic Situation Improves; Capital Flows Back and Government Bonds Rise 79

Brussels: The State Council met today to discuss the financial and economic situation. They are quite satisfied with the recent capital flow situation. Since the establishment of the new cabinet, the total amount of capital flowing into Belgium has exceeded 2 billion Belgian francs. In other words, the capital that flowed out in January of this year has now returned to Belgium. The prices of various government bonds continue to rise, forcing the government to release huge amounts of bonds to meet public demand. Due to the increase in government bond prices, the government may implement interest rate swaps in the near future. In addition, the increase in savings deposits is also a welcome phenomenon. Savings have increased by 50 million Belgian francs in the past two weeks. The most important issue currently being studied by the government is whether to respect or abandon gold clauses in private contracts. The government will announce its decision tomorrow. It is estimated that most debts will abandon gold clauses, but bondholders of loans from the United States will still be repaid principal and interest in accordance with the gold standard within one year. (Havas, 8th)

Roosevelt Signs: The American Works Relief Act is Implemented 80

(Washington) President Roosevelt signed the $4.88 billion Works Relief Act today on a train from Jacksonville to New York. The purpose of this act is to place millions of unemployed people with wages lower than the current wages in private industry. The law stipulates that the maximum monthly wage should not exceed $50 in order to avoid direct competition between the country and private individuals. This case was put into effect today. Gold and Silver

British Gold: London gold prices fell by 9.5 pence today due to the rise in the pound, to 144 shillings and 1.5 pence.

Northwestern Inspection Notes 107

— Special Correspondent Geng Ya

My First Encounter with Robbers

As the sky was beginning to lighten, the car drove out of Dingcheng. After twenty-four kilometers, we reached Hongtuyao. There were dozens of households of residents, with piles of wheat stacked like green mushrooms from afar. The clouds were dim, the morning sun was shining through them, and the cold wind was biting to the bone. We drove for seven or eight kilometers on the plain, then began to ascend Huajialing. The passengers slowly took the shortcut, panting and their legs aching. The car swerved left and right, sometimes going up and then retreating. If wooden chocks were not used to block the wheels, it would have rolled straight into the deep ravine. Upon reaching the high ridge, we got into the car and looked around. Mountains and valleys were laid out beneath our feet. White clouds swirled around the car, with small snowflakes gathering in the clouds, hitting our faces softly, as if there was something and nothing at all. After passing a high mountain pass, we traveled along the ridge, with deep ravines and dangerous cliffs on both sides. The fog became thicker, and the car drove slower. I felt uneasy in my heart, as if walking on the edge of a deep abyss. Suddenly, two cars came towards us, their horns blaring loudly, faintly heard from within the fog, and then quickly disappearing into the clouds again. The passengers all huddled and shrunk their necks, covered in snow. We expected the east side of the ridge to be a silver world, as we had already seen the signs. Huajialing is one hundred kilometers long. After traveling about a third of the way, we indeed entered a silver world. The clouds and fog were still thick, and it was still snowing. Everything, from trees to grass, was transformed into silver by the clouds and fog, which was completely different from the snow-covered trees on the plains, with only a few pear blossoms blooming. Just as we were enjoying the snow scenery, we suddenly heard two "bang" sounds, and the car stopped abruptly. At first, we suspected that a tire had burst, but then we heard shouts of "Get down, get down!" We then saw two people standing four or five steps in front of the car, wearing long gowns and short jackets, with robes on their shoulders. Each of them held a pistol and fired into the air. They continued to shout at the passengers, "Get down quickly! We are just borrowing some travel expenses from you." The passengers were shocked to learn that they had encountered robbers and were all terrified. The truck had no windows, so everyone jumped out one after another, their feet heavy and their eyes averted, staring in shock. Another three robbers, all dressed as travelers, but without guns, only carrying walking sticks, ordered everyone to quickly line up and hand over their valuables one by one. The robbers took them and threw them into bags, the sound of silver coins hitting each other ringing in the air. The robbers even felt the clothes of those who were more richly dressed. A missionary repeatedly begged, "You (referring to the robbers) are robbing the rich to help the poor, I am acting on behalf of heaven!" The robbers ignored him and robbed him of his silver in the end.

I was standing at the end of the line. Although I had brought some travel expenses with me, they were all ten-yuan banknotes and small denominations. Silver coins were too heavy, so I had put them in my briefcase. Also, because the map had fallen into the water last night, I had wrapped the briefcase in my luggage this morning. Therefore, I had no silver coins with me at this time to deal with the situation. If I wanted to take out the banknotes, I would have to move the whole amount, otherwise it would be better not to give anything, and perhaps I could be spared. Thinking of this, the robbers had already searched up to me. In my panic, I did not know what to do. I slightly patted my breast pocket to show that I had nothing. The robber reached into my pocket and mistook my diary for a wallet. He pulled it out and looked at it, then handed it back. I had just returned from outside the Guan (Shanhaiguan Pass), wearing a "locomotive hat," an old cloth leather robe, and not a penny in my pocket. The robbers did not suspect me, so I was unexpectedly spared. Then, one of the robbers jumped onto the car, threw the luggage to the ground, and ordered everyone to step back so they could unpack and inspect it.

Forced by the robbers, everyone lowered their heads and stepped back. Those who had silver coins in their luggage were all anxious at this point. Just as the situation was critical, the truck of the Gansu Provincial Anti-Opium Committee rushed from the snow and fog. A passenger ran to inform them that there were robbers. The three soldiers in the truck immediately got out with live ammunition. Seeing that the incoming vehicle had guns, the robbers shouted to each other to quickly escape down the slope. The snow was deep and the fog was thick, and they disappeared in an instant. The other cars continued to arrive, but did not pursue them, firing dozens of shots into the air. The valley echoed with loud sounds. After a while, there was barking from dogs about two or three miles down the mountain. It was likely that there were villages, and the robbers had already escaped.

About five or six bags of luggage were thrown down from the car, but only two were unpacked. A pair of new "Suzhou jiawowo" shoes (a type of shoe with a thick sole of two inches, black woolen edges, and red woolen faces, specially worn in winter to keep warm) and a pair of glasses were taken away. Although my luggage was also thrown to the ground, it was not unpacked. Otherwise, my briefcase or camera would have been snatched away. Assuming that the robbers would not attack again, we packed up and continued on. Although several people had their travel expenses stolen, the robbers did not hurt anyone, which was fortunate. I had previously passed through a mountain on the border of Gansu and Ningxia and Xingxing Gorge on the border of Gansu and Xinjiang, and although I had heard about robbers twice, I had not actually encountered a dangerous situation. This encounter at Huajialing can be said to be my first. Life's journey is never smooth. Looking back on it now, it is quite interesting.

After a hurried drive through the snow, we arrived at a village also named Huajialing. According to the local people, "The place where we were robbed is called Haojia Qu Liangzi. Shajiawan, thirty miles to the east, also often experiences robberies." After passing Shajiawan, the terrain became very steep, but fortunately, nothing happened. We traveled along the ridge, and it was already night. The snow reflected the light, and the sky was dark gray. We circled down a steep slope. The first car had people treading through the snow to find the way, while the cars behind followed the tracks slowly. We arrived at Jieshipu at 11:00 PM and stayed overnight. The journey was one hundred and fifty kilometers. There was a company of soldiers stationed in the village, with over seventy households of residents. We departed early the next morning at sunrise. After passing Qijia Mountain, we traveled fifteen kilometers to Jingning County. The shops were lined up neatly, and the population was prosperous. After the snow, the earth houses and dead branches were all transformed into jade trees and jade buildings. The sunlight shone brightly, like rain. The car stopped for two hours to pick up new passengers. Taking advantage of the time, I visited County Magistrate Xu Junchong, intending to inquire about the local situation. I waited in the reception room and saw a sign on the wall that read, "By strict order of the Suiyuan Office, the county government must not provide the army with any miscellaneous services..." But the messenger handed my name card inside, and then led a quartermaster in. I secretly guessed that this rule was ineffective. After a while, the messenger came out and suddenly asked me, "Did you just arrive here from Lanzhou by car?" I answered yes. He then said, "The county magistrate has gone out." Later, I returned to the station and learned that Mr. Yang, who was traveling with me, had been robbed of everything on the way and had given the county magistrate three yuan as a gift. No wonder my subsequent visit caused a misunderstanding and I was turned away. At 1:00 PM, the car continued eastward.

Xu Xiangqian's Bandits Surrounded in Sichuan; Fuling River Defenses Secure Western Sichuan; Wang, Deng, and Hu's Armies Join Forces to Suppress 108

Hankou Communication - Xu Xiangqian's remnant bandits, after fleeing from Southern Shaanxi back to Northern Sichuan, launched a full-scale attack on Guangyuan and Zhaohua, but were repelled by the combined forces of Deng Xihou and Tian Songyao. Unexpectedly, Cangxi was poorly defended, and the bandit troops secretly crossed the Jialing River, continuing to expand into Western Sichuan. Upon receiving the report in Guizhou, Chairman Chiang immediately dismissed Tian Songyao from his post and increased troop reinforcements to suppress the bandits. The various armies engaged in suppression have been winning battles in recent days. In addition to Wang Zanxu's Fifth Route Army having occupied Southern City and advancing victoriously towards Suining, Deng's army on the eastern bank of the Fuling River has also engaged in fierce battles with the bandits. Deng has built bunkers and strengthened fortifications along the Fuling River. The rear troops are completely concentrated in Mianyang, while the front lines are guarding Zitong, preventing the bandits from advancing west. On the 5th, Xu's bandits, with a large force, advanced from Maying Temple and Wulianyi towards the D묘ao Mountain east of Zitong, engaging in a fierce battle with the Huang Division and Che Cheng regiments of Deng's army for a full day and night. The bandits suffered heavy casualties and retreated to Maying Temple and Wulianyi. Currently, Hu Zongnan's division has recovered Ningqiang and is stationed in Guangyuan, effectively coordinating with the Chen Dingxun and Yang Xiuchun divisions of Deng's army, agreeing on a date to jointly suppress the bandits. Upon investigation, the bandits' westward escape was due to being besieged on all sides, fleeing desperately without any plan. They are now trapped in a four-sided encirclement. Not only is Western Sichuan secure, but the elimination of the remnant bandits is also possible. (8th)

Wuhu Meat Industry Strike; Opposing 30% Surtax for Compulsory Education 109

Wuhu Communication - Funds for compulsory education in Wuhu were previously stipulated to be surcharged on slaughter taxes. Since the great flood in 1931, the slaughterers have been unable to pay according to the regulations due to poor business, and the Meat Industry Association has recognized and paid 1,000 yuan annually. Recently, the education authorities, believing that the compulsory education funds were still severely inadequate, decided through the finance and education departments to order Wuhu County to stop the recognized payment method and instead surcharge 30% of the regular tax (i.e., 1.2 cents surcharge on every 4 cents of regular tax). However, the meat industry believes that it is a small-scale operation that can barely make a living, and the value of a pig is only about 10 yuan, while the taxes and levies they bear include 4 cents for slaughter tax, 1.6 cents for livestock tax, and 0.6 cents for meat levy. Now, with such a heavy surcharge, it amounts to more than 60/1000th of the business tax. At a time when excessive taxes and levies are being abolished, and the Provincial Tax Supervision Committee has been newly established, they are demanding to continue the previous practice of total payment by the association and to withdraw the order to surcharge 30%. The county government believes that this is a decision made by the provincial government and is uniform across all counties, so it cannot be changed easily and is difficult to approve. Therefore, the entire meat industry went on strike today and petitioned the central government according to the law, hoping to achieve their goal. It has been reported that Zhang Yuanda and Ma Wushan, two business owners, have been detained by the local tax bureau and sent to the county government for custody because they are unable to recognize and pay the surcharge. (8th)

Songjiang; Knife-Wounded Male Corpse Discovered in Shengxiang 110

On the 5th, an unidentified male corpse was discovered by the riverbank in the Luye Tang area of Shengxiang, Tianma Mountain. The corpse was about thirty years old, wearing a dark blue lined robe, dark blue wool trousers, and a yellow shirt. He had a pair of plain glasses and a box of cigarettes in his possession, with a cigarette held between his fingers. There was a knife wound to the forehead, throat, bridge of the nose (two wounds), and back. There were three knife wounds to the body. The death was gruesome, clearly a revenge killing. However, no one knew the name of the corpse. The local village police reported it to the Tianma Mountain Public Security Station and then to the Songjiang Bureau, and sent a letter to the County Court Prosecutor's Office. On the 9th, the prosecutor led officials and police to hire a boat to go to the countryside to conduct an inspection in order to thoroughly investigate the matter.

Suzhou; Elder Gentleman Fei Zhongshen Passes Away 111

Fei Zhongshen (Shuwei), a resident of Taohuawu in Suzhou, was a gentleman from Wujiang. He was 52 years old. During the reign of Yuan Shikai, Fei served as a Censor. His eldest daughter-in-law is Yuan Shikai's granddaughter. Fei was recently deeply stimulated by the issue of Wujiang County's collection of outstanding taxes and suddenly suffered a stroke a few days ago. Despite extensive treatment by famous doctors, he died at 9:00 PM on the 8th. The coffin will be sealed on the 11th. Fei was usually enthusiastic about social welfare and charitable causes and was the founder of the Suzhou Electric Power Plant. Therefore, the local people deeply regret his passing.

Robbers Encountered on Return Boat from Watching a Play 112

In the eighteenth du, fifth qu, of Taiping Bridge Township in the rural area of Suzhou, farmers from the entire village performed plays for two days on the sixth and seventh days [of the month] to thank the gods for preventing blight. Six or seven villagers from nearby Wu Ta Township traveled by boat to Taiping Bridge Township to watch the plays. On the seventh, on their return journey in the evening, as they passed the Big Pond, they encountered a sudden downpour. Suddenly, a robber boat appeared, carrying seven or eight robbers, each armed with guns, who intercepted them and robbed them. They were robbed of jewelry and silver dollars worth approximately one hundred yuan and fled towards Changshu. Furthermore, Wang Bao, a housewife who owned a sundry goods store in the fifth tu of the eleventh du of Fengqiao Township, was robbed some days ago. The robbers burned Wang Bao's lower body with fire, and she died of severe injuries on the afternoon of the eighth due to the fire poisoning her heart. The local prosecutor's office sent personnel on the ninth to examine the body.

Wuxi: Telegram Requesting Rejection of Increased Cotton Tax 114

The Cotton Textile Trade Association of this city previously telegraphed a request to the Central Government to severely reprimand the Cotton Merchants for submitting a request to the Central Government to increase import cotton taxes. The Chinese Cotton Mill United Association also telegraphed, insisting on a unified position. Yesterday, it convened a general membership meeting. After discussion, it was resolved that expensive cotton and cheap yarn have brought Chinese cotton mills to the brink of total collapse. Although cotton prices are now low, they are still higher than foreign cotton. Taxes should be reduced immediately; there is no reason to increase them. This association should telegraph the Nanjing Executive Yuan, Ministry of Finance, and Ministry of Industry, severely requesting them to reject the request.

Large Quantities of Foreign Rice Arrive in Wuxi for Sale 115

Recently, in the rice market of this city, the inferior grades of粳 and 秈 rice are about to be sold out. Shipments from various places are mostly high-grade, so the price of rice has risen by seven or eight jiao compared to half a month ago. Recently, although large quantities of foreign rice have arrived in Wuxi by boat, the market price has not been affected. Most of the foreign rice ordered by this city from Shanghai is futures, with the original price being 5.45 yuan per hundred jin. Calculated in local dou and hu, the price is equivalent to 11.5 yuan per shi. The current price of foreign rice in the Wuxi market is 9.45 yuan per shi. If the sellers were to sell at the current market price, they would lose more than 2 yuan per shi. Because foreign rice can be stored for a long time, they are unwilling to sell it off quickly and plan to store it in warehouses, observing the market situation before selling.

Changzhou: Joint Survey of County Boundaries by Wu and Dan Counties Results in Dispute 116

Yu Village in the third district of Wu County was recently being organized into baojia by Wu Zongjin, the district head of that district. Jiang Ke, the district head of the fifth district of Danyang County, also went to organize baojia, resulting in a dispute. District Head Wu of Wu County immediately drew a map and attached a certificate of proof, submitting it to the county government for instructions. County Magistrate Hou immediately sent a letter to the Danyang County government requesting verification and correction. Yesterday, the Danyang County government replied, stating that the county boundary in that area seemed to be quite different. For the sake of caution, each county should send one committee member to conduct an on-the-spot survey with the district offices of both counties. County Magistrate Hou immediately appointed Yue Jun and scheduled to go for a joint survey on the twelfth of this month. He also sent a letter to the Danyang County government requesting that a committee member be sent to arrive at the disputed location at that time for an on-the-spot survey so that a decision could be made.

Zhenjiang: Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance Recovers Management of Tobacco and Alcohol License Taxes from Various Counties and Manages it Directly 117

After the tobacco and alcohol license tax was transferred from the Ministry of Finance to the provinces for management, Zhejiang Province set up a bureau to manage it by commission, and the results were the best. Anhui Province also achieved effective results by having the business tax bureau handle it concurrently. After Jiangsu Province took over in July of last year, Gu Baoyu used the names of the tobacco and alcohol associations of Shanghai and Ningbo to contract for the entire year's tax revenue of Jiangsu Province for 760,000 yuan. The actual tax amount to be paid annually was 680,000 yuan, divided into four seasons and paid monthly. A general bureau was established in Zhenjiang, and branch bureaus were established in various districts, which were then subcontracted to others. After half a year of operation, some branch bureaus embezzled funds and fled, some failed to remit funds, and some collected excess taxes and refused to hand them over. Within eight months, the general bureau only submitted more than 130,000 yuan to the Department of Finance, which was not even enough for one quarter's quota. The Department of Finance feared that this would drag on, causing more and more disputes, making it more and more difficult to rectify. Therefore, last month, it resolutely recovered the management of famous counties south of the Yangtze River and commissioned the business tax bureaus of each county to handle it concurrently. Meanwhile, it sent personnel to various counties to investigate. If there were cases of poor management and complex content, even if the contract period had not ended, the business tax bureau was ordered to take over. Strict orders were given to recover the accumulated tax arrears in various districts. Currently, except for the second and sixth districts, which are still contracted by Gu Baoyu, all other counties have been taken back by the Department of Finance and ordered to be handled concurrently by the business tax bureau.

Jiaxing: Rioters Snatch Rice and Assault Police 118

In Tudiansi Town, Tongxiang, yesterday and the day before, when a charity was distributing rations to disaster victims repatriated from Songjiang at the town's defense corps, they were suddenly robbed by a large number of rioters who also assaulted the police and defense corps. Local News

Song Ziwen Announces: Government's Increase in Capital for Bank of China Focuses Entirely on Policy, Not Personnel; Future Business Strategy Will Be Entirely Commercialized 125

According to the Central News Agency, Song Ziwen, Standing Committee Member of the National Economic Council and Chairman of the Board of Directors of the Bank of China, met with reporters from various newspapers at the Bank of China at 10:00 a.m. yesterday to announce the government's original intention in increasing the capital of the Bank of China and the Bank's future business strategy. The following is a record of Song's conversation:

Government's Capital Increase: Focus on Policy

According to Song, the government's increase in capital for the Bank of China and the appointment of himself here is entirely focused on policy, not personnel. He himself came here to promote the government's policy. Since taking office, he has not brought a single person with him. The Bank of China has a wealth of talent. He hopes that he will never send another person here in the future. All of the Bank's staff are working as usual. This shows that all of the Bank's staff understand the government's intentions. Previously, the general public did not understand the reasons for the changes in the Bank of China and rumored that the Bank's credit would not be as stable as before. However, to date, the deposits of the Bank and its branches have not decreased, and new depositors are constantly arriving. All of these facts are well known to the Bank of China's more than 2,000 employees and colleagues in the financial sector. This further shows that the society has also understood the government's intentions.

Bank of China's Future Business Strategy

The Bank of China's future business strategy will be entirely commercialized, eliminating all bureaucratic habits, and striving for international exchange and focusing on import and export trade, without conflicting with the Central Bank. This will allow each bank to develop its business with its own strength. Mr. Song Hanzhang forcefully prevented the Bank of China's banknotes from ceasing to be convertible during the Yuan Shikai era. This time, he was appointed as the General Manager of the Bank of China, which is fortunate. As for the government-appointed official shareholder directors, such as Qian Xinzhi, Ye Zhuotang, Wu Daquan, Hu Bijiang, and Wang Baolun, are all members of the business community. This further confirms that the government's changes to the Bank of China are entirely focused on policy, not personnel.

Song Denies Economic Control

Song denied the rumors that the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications would implement economic control after increasing their capital. He said that the government's increase in capital for the three banks is still based on the policy set in 1929. The Central Bank is the national bank, acting as the national treasury for revenue and expenditure. The Bank of China focuses on international exchange, and the Bank of Communications develops industries. This has not changed.

Promoting Relief for Industry and Commerce

Regarding the issue of alleviating the decline of industry and commerce, the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications are discussing the implementation so that the industry and commerce on the verge of collapse can have the hope of recovery in a short period of time. As for the 5 million yuan small loan for industrial and commercial credit, which is half undertaken by the Ministry of Finance and half by the banking community, is also being actively promoted. Song said that he had not heard of the rumor that the government would control the issuance of banknotes. He thought this was referring to provincial banks, not commercial banks.

Inspection of Branches: Postponing Trip to Sichuan

Song was originally scheduled to go to Sichuan for inspection in the coming days, but due to taking office as Chairman of the Board of Directors of the Bank of China, various matters are waiting to be handled. Therefore, he cannot spare the time to go to Sichuan for the time being. He plans to go to various branches for inspection after the matters of the head office are handled properly. It has not yet been decided whether his itinerary will first go to Pingjin. It is also learned that Song is scheduled to host a banquet at the head office on the tenth to celebrate with the bank staff.

Wang's Remarks

When Wang arrived in Shanghai, he told reporters on the ship that his inspection trip was very good. The situation of the declining business of overseas Chinese. In the past, the sugar merchants of Java, the rubber merchants of Singapore, the rice merchants of Saigon, and the import and export merchants of Manila were most affected by the global economic depression, but since this year, it has been better than last year, and there is a great hope of revival in the future. As for Singapore, Wang said that the preparations of the British for future world wars are military secrets and he is not at liberty to talk about them, but we can guess without asking, and know the general idea. The independence movement in the Philippines is now in full swing and will be realized next spring. It is generally believed that the first president will undoubtedly be former Speaker Quezon.

Qian Industry to Hold Executive Committee Meeting Today to Discuss Old Loans: Factories' Request for Extension May Be Difficult to Grant 129

According to the Shiye News Agency, the Shanghai Money Trade Association has been implementing the small loan for industrial and commercial credit relief case in accordance with the resolutions of the members' meeting to do their best and not to join the banking consortium. However, the old loans must still be paid on time in order to benefit both parties. Now, the association has received a letter from the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, stating that various factories and shops have requested a lenient approach for the long-term loans (i.e., old loans) that are about to expire, before the small credit loan and mortgage loan have been announced and implemented. The Committee for the Promotion of National Goods also sent a letter requesting an extension of the payment period. Qin Runqing, chairman of the association, believed that the matter was of great importance to the future of the industry and could not be answered casually. In order to handle the matter carefully, it was decided to convene the 37th meeting of the 2nd Executive Committee at the Ningbo Road Association at 2:00 p.m. today (the 10th) to publicly discuss the requests of the two parties. According to the spokesperson of the association, the old loans are collected according to the regulations on the due date in both directions. The industry also receives the amount of money according to the budget in order to meet the future borrowers, and the business can be turned around and extended. If the above requirements are followed, it is tantamount to helping others while endangering oneself. It is heard that today's meeting may not approve the request for an extension of the loan.

Commercial Acceptance Draft: Banking Association Approves Principles 130

According to the Guowen News Agency, the Shanghai Banking Association held its 65th Executive Committee meeting at 4:00 p.m. yesterday and made decisions on small credit loans and commercial acceptance drafts. The details are recorded below:

Attending Committee Members

Yesterday was the 65th Executive Committee meeting, attached with the 63rd Standing Committee meeting. In addition to the Standing Executive Committee members, representatives of all member banks were also present. Those present were Tang Shoumin, Li Fukun, Xu Jilong, Xu Xinliu, Ye Fuxiao, Chen Zheqing, Qu Jigang, Hu Bijiang, Chen Guangfu, Wu Yunzhai, Jing Runshi, Bei Songsun, Wang Yansong, Xu Boming, Wang Boyuan, Huang Mohan, Liu Huizhi, Hu Xinan, Le Gengrong, Liu Hongyuan, Sun Jingxi, Wu Weiru, Qi Yunqing, Wang Zhihua, Yao Yinpeng, Lin Yibo, Zhu Zikui, Chen Shizhen, Zhu Huisheng, Wei Jinsan, Zhang Zhuru, Dong Xianting, and Secretary-General Lin Kanghou, etc., totaling 33 people. Chen Guangfu presided over the meeting, Gu Chengan recorded, and the ceremony was performed as usual. First, the resolutions of the 64th Executive Committee and the 62nd Standing Committee meetings were reported, and then the discussion began.

Credit Loan

(1) The case of how to handle the fact that the number of small industrial and commercial credit loans reported by various banks is close to 2 million yuan was resolved and referred to the nine-bank task force committee appointed by the last Executive Committee to formulate implementation methods. According to a committee member who attended the meeting, the original number of small credit loans was 5 million yuan, which was equally divided between the government and the banking industry. Although Minister Kong orally agreed to the government's 2.5 million yuan, he has not yet replied. The banking industry has also not agreed to undertake 500,000 yuan. Now the banking industry has already raised the original number of 2 million yuan, which can be raised. If the facts are urgent, it may first undertake the number that has been raised, but it still needs to be adapted to the times and carefully studied by the task force committee.

Acceptance Draft

(2) The case of the Acceptance Draft Task Force Committee's deliberation and approval of six principles for the acceptance draft discount business (the original text is recorded later) was resolved and approved as is, and the association will handle it separately. (3) The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the association, requesting the formulation of a method for discounting commercial acceptance drafts and appointing representatives for consultation. It was resolved to recommend Jing Runshi of the Bank of China and Xue Yisheng of the Bank of Communications to attend as representatives. Other cases were also discussed and the meeting adjourned at 5:30 p.m.

Six Principles

The six principles for the commercial acceptance draft discount business are as follows: (1) Gradually replace credit overdraft loans with acceptance drafts. (2) The association should submit a request to the Ministry of Finance, approving the discounting of these bills to be used as reserve for issuance. (3) Please ask the Central Bank to publicly determine the discount rate daily and post it so that each bank can determine its own discount rate. This discount rate should be lower than the credit overdraft rate. (4) After each bank receives the discount, it can rediscount with each other, and finally rediscount with the Central Bank. (5) When each bank receives the acceptance draft discount business, if it needs to investigate with its peers, it is hoped that each bank will report the facts as much as possible. (6) If the bill is refused payment upon maturity, the discounting bank shall be obligated to report to its peers.

Money Industry Research

A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency learned from the money industry yesterday that Article 4, Paragraph 4 of Chapter 3 of the Shanghai Money Trade Industry Regulations, the Scope of Business, has a provision for "the discounting of various term bills." However, although there is the above provision, each money shop is very cautious about discounting term bills. It does not discount to unfamiliar customers in order to prevent abuses. As for the issue of discounting commercial acceptance drafts, the Money Trade Association has submitted a request to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to formulate discounting methods, and has submitted them for detailed study. After a considerable decision is made, it will be submitted to the members' representatives' standing committee for discussion. As for the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, it has decided to wait for the banking and money industries to submit the names of their representatives before convening a joint meeting of the representatives of the banking and money industries to make a decision.

Northwest Research Association The Northwest Problem Research Association held a farewell banquet for Envoy He at the Bank Club on Hong Kong Road at 3:00 PM yesterday afternoon. Turkey is striving for rejuvenation, and its previous status was similar to that of our country. We hope that Envoy He will report Turkey's diplomatic, political, economic, and educational regulations to our government and people for reference." Mr. He then gave a reply, which is omitted.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Last night at 6:00 PM, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce hosted a farewell banquet for Mr. He. More than twenty people attended, including Wang Xiaofan, Chen Zheqing, Wu Xingya, Pan Gongzhan, Xiong Xiling, Du Yuesheng, and Shen Tianxin. Xiong Shaokang, Chairman of the Guangzhou Municipal Chamber of Commerce, happened to be in Shanghai and was also invited to the banquet. Chairman Chen Zheqing delivered a speech, saying, "Envoy He Guiyan is a senior figure in the military. Initially, he led divisions and participated in the Northern Expedition of the 16th year of the Republic of China under the command of Chairman Jiang, for which he was credited with meritorious service. Later, he defended the capital, planned strategies, and his scholarly military demeanor was renowned in the world. Our chamber has long admired your brilliance but has not had the opportunity to express our sentiments. Now, we are fortunate to witness your appointment as envoy to Turkey. Your carriage is about to depart, and you are passing through Shanghai, allowing our colleagues to raise a glass and have a good meeting, which we deeply appreciate. Our chamber still remembers that when our country first established diplomatic relations with foreign countries, most of those selected were sought from the Hanlin Academy. Later, as translation talents emerged, they were selected from the Tongwen Guan and Guang Fangyan Guan. Recently, those familiar with military strategy and knowledgeable about foreign situations have been appointed, integrating literary and military skills, both internal and external, into one. Envoys such as Envoy Jiang stationed in Japan and Envoy Liu stationed in Germany have already added luster. Today, you, sir, form a tripod with them, truly showing that the country has no shortage of talent and is gradually restoring the grand tradition of the Zhou Dynasty, where literary and military affairs were not separated, which is truly gratifying. Turkey had exchanges with China as early as the Tang Dynasty and is China's oldest neighbor, but it has only established diplomatic relations with our country in recent years, making it our newest neighbor. Its people are known in history for their agility, bravery, and resistance to foreign tribes, and the country's Grand President Kemal rose from the military, and his civil and military achievements shine in the Near East, which our country envies. As for commercial relations with our country, because that country has never been known for its business acumen, although it has also followed the Soviet Union's policy of state-run industries in recent years and strived for self-sufficiency, its relationship with our country is still shallow, and the volume of goods imported and exported each year is minimal. Therefore, the duties of our country's envoy to Turkey in the future are not so much about developing trade between the two countries as about closely observing the national situation, understanding their strengths, and choosing the best to follow. Our chamber has repeatedly heard Envoy He's lectures on the situation in Turkey when he was in Beijing and Shanghai, which can be described as knowing them like the back of his hand. Even experts specializing in international affairs cannot surpass his knowledge. Our chamber is pleased that the country has found the right person and also remembers that our country is still unable to shake off the nickname of 'Sick Man of the Far East,' which is similar to the way Europeans used to regard Turkey as the 'Sick Man of the Near East.' We deeply hope that Envoy He can do his best to observe the country's affairs and provide good advice, providing a reference for our country's revitalization, then Envoy He's trip will be a great contribution to the party and the country, and he will receive no small reward. Our chamber respectfully offers a toast at the time of your departure, wishing you success on this trip." (Mr. He's reply is omitted.)

Second Day of the Art Exhibition Preview More Visitors Than the Previous Day 133

Central News Agency reports that yesterday was the second day of the Shanghai preview of the London Exhibition of Chinese Art. Although the weather was cloudy, because there was no rain, the number of visitors was even greater than the previous day, with more foreigners than Chinese and more women than men. The praise for our country's ancient art filled the entire venue. A reporter from the Central News Agency specially recorded the various situations yesterday as follows:

Transportation Ship Not Yet Determined

The antiques for this exhibition will be carefully packed after the closing and handed over to a British special warship for transportation to London for exhibition. Currently, the British side has designated the HMS Suffolk to come to Shanghai for transport. The ship is one of the British Asian Fleet and is currently anchored off the Bund in the French Concession. Yesterday morning at 10:30 AM, under the guidance of British representative Mr. Raffael, the secretary of the exhibition, Tang Xifen, and Zhuang Shangyan, together with a delegation from the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company led by Wei Huanzhang, went to visit the ship. Wei is well-versed in maritime transportation. The ship's captain, Mr. Manners, warmly received them, offered wine and food, and guided them to visit the entire ship and warehouse. The ship is about 10,000 tons, more than seven hundred feet long, and the hull is very narrow, so it travels very fast, reaching about thirty knots per hour. They returned to the exhibition at about 11:00 AM. In the afternoon at 3:00 PM, Captain Manners also visited the exhibition for three hours before returning to the ship. As to whether the ship is suitable for transporting antiques, the person in charge of the exhibition has not yet agreed to announce it, but it is said that the ship vibrates slightly when traveling at a considerable speed, and this time the ship is returning to England for rest and will go directly to Portsmouth instead of London. Therefore, the route to be taken for the transportation of antiques to England in the future is still unknown.

Art School Students Visit

Yesterday morning, more than fifty students from the Hangzhou National Academy of Art, led by the Dean of Academic Affairs, came to Shanghai specifically to purchase tickets to enter the venue and visit for a long time. The order at the exhibition was also very good, and the audience paid great attention to conversations and footsteps.

Zheng Tianxi Attends

According to the exhibition, (1) In the section of calligraphy, two paintings by Lang Shining were selected. Lang was originally Italian. The English catalog originally transliterated Lang's name according to Chinese pronunciation. Now it has been changed to Lang's original Italian name, Castiglione Girseppe. (2) Copperware No. 80 was originally "Rhino Zun," now changed to "Sacrificial Zun." (3) Zheng Tianxi, the Chinese special envoy for the London Art Exhibition, was at the exhibition all day yesterday, discussing the export of antiques with the managers of the exhibition. (4) Many people visited the exhibition yesterday, half of whom were Westerners, including antique dealers carefully appreciating and evaluating the exhibits, believing that the exhibits were indeed Chinese treasures.

Page 12

Social Affairs Bureau Advocates for the Establishment of Labor-Farmer Cooperatives (Continued) 135

(2) Promotion of Rural Cooperation

Implementation Steps

This city is an industrial and commercial area and is not known for agriculture. However, in terms of the area of farmland in this city, it accounts for about three-fifths of the city's area, and the number of farmers accounts for more than one-tenth of the city's total population. Moreover, due to the international economic pressure and the prevalence of natural disasters in recent years, the rural areas of this city are on the verge of bankruptcy. Rural areas and cities have interconnected economic relations, and rescuing rural areas is an important political task at present. There are many ways to rescue them, but the most important and easy way is to promote rural cooperation. The bureau, in view of this, has specially formulated the "Outline of the Rural Cooperative Plan of this City" and the "Rural Cooperative Experimental Area Plan of this City" to promote it, and the municipal government has raised 80,000 yuan for the rural cooperative loan fund for the lending of cooperatives and for economic assistance. In addition, three rural cooperative instructors were extended to investigate the rural situation and take responsibility for guiding the cooperatives. Now, the Yinhang District is designated as an experimental area for active implementation, hoping to achieve twice the result with half the effort.

Plan Outline

Shanghai Rural Cooperative Plan Outline: (1) The rural areas of this city include Gaoqiao, Tangqiao, Jiangwan, Gaoxing, Zhenru, Lixing, Wusong, Pengpu, Yinhang, Pusong, Fahua, Caojing, Yangsi, Zhabei, Yinxiang, and Yangjing, a total of seventeen districts. Except for Zhabei, Hunan, Yinxiang, and Yangjing, four districts which are mostly industrial and commercial areas, the remaining thirteen districts are places where farmers are concentrated. It is decided to set up one cooperative in each district, and sub-branches can be set up in various townships according to actual needs. (2) The rural cooperatives in each district are set as both-operating nature, and their business includes credit purchase, sales, utilization of production, etc., depending on the economic situation of each district, to determine which business is important, which business is secondary, which should be done first, and which can be done slowly. The bureau and the municipal agricultural association and municipal commissioners from each district will send personnel to various townships to promote, so that farmers understand the benefits of the cooperative and help them organize. (3) The business of rural cooperatives in each district will be conducted according to the needs of each district. However, in order to seek the stability and development of the cooperative, the government authorities should allocate loan funds to the rural cooperatives in this city to use them as a turnover, so that their capital will not be exhausted. According to the current local situation in this city, there are seventeen townships. Except for the four districts that are industrial and commercial areas where the establishment will be postponed, the remaining thirteen districts should be established in phases. Each district should set up one cooperative and four sub-branches, then thirteen districts should set up thirteen cooperatives and fifty-two sub-branches. If the loan for each district cooperative is assumed to be 5,000 yuan, then the thirteen districts will total 65,000 yuan, plus a reserve of 15,000 yuan, a total of 80,000 yuan is required. (4) The cooperative loan fund of 80,000 yuan is designated to be kept by the Municipal Bank of this city, and the Social Affairs Bureau formulates measures for phased lending, but only to legally registered rural cooperatives, and those who have not registered shall not request loans. (5) It is practically difficult to hold rural cooperatives in the thirteen townships of this city at the same time. Now, it is planned to handle them in phases. The first phase is Lixing, Yangsi, Wusong, Pengpu; the second phase is Gaoxing, Yinhang, Pusong, Gaoqiao; the third phase is Caojing, Fahua, Jiangwan, Tangqiao, Zhenru. (6) The preparation period for each phase is pre-determined to be three months to six months. During this period, the bureau and the municipal agricultural association and the municipal commissioners of each district are responsible for the preparation and urge the establishment of rural cooperatives in each district on time. (7) The term of the loan shall not exceed one year, but an extension may be applied for, limited to once. The standard of loan interest is 6% per annum. The loan procedures are based on the following restrictions in principle, but may be changed according to the economic situation of each cooperative: (1) Within the first two years of the establishment of a rural cooperative, the funds released by the community to its members and the needs for handling various businesses may request full borrowing. (2) After the establishment of the cooperative, starting from the third year, the funds released by the community to its members and other business needs may request borrowing up to seven-tenths of the total amount, and the rest should be raised by the community. (3) After the establishment of the cooperative, starting from the fifth year, the funds released by the community to its members and other business needs may request borrowing up to four-tenths of the total amount, and the rest should be raised by the community. (4) After the cooperative has been established for seven years, it should raise funds to handle various businesses, and shall not request loans unless necessary. (5) Cooperative loans are not limited to cash, and may be allocated according to the price of farmers' needs, such as fertilizers, agricultural tools, and seeds. (6) The types and procedures for lending shall be formulated by the Social Affairs Bureau and submitted to the Municipal Government for approval. (The Shanghai Rural Cooperative Experimental Area Plan has been detailed in previous reports.) (End)

Ministry of Communications Building a Mansion in Shanghai Re-progressing According to the Original Plan 137

Central News Agency reports that in order to facilitate its operations, the Ministry of Communications had planned to rebuild the Communications Building on the original site of the Telegraph Bureau on Sichuan Road and Fourth Road, so that all agencies of the Ministry in Shanghai could move in uniformly. However, due to various reasons, it has not been realized. However, this matter is now being re-progressed because the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau will no longer move to Beijing. It is learned that all construction will be based on the original plan, and the Telegraph Bureau and the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau will move in first. If there are any remaining rooms, other agencies of the Ministry of Communications in Shanghai will be planned to move in for office work. It is estimated that the Telegraph Bureau will need four floors, and the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau will need two floors. The mansion was originally planned for twelve floors, so it is expected that there will be remaining rooms allocated to other agencies of the Ministry of Communications for use. As for the construction funds, they have also been settled and are being actively planned so that they can be realized as soon as possible.

They also discussed the solicitation of aviation salvation donations. For rental trucks for transporting goods and moving venues, 2% should be collected from customers according to the standard of business volume, and the minimum limit of 6 yuan per vehicle should be collected per month. For trucks for transporting goods and moving venues prepared by themselves, 6 yuan should be donated per month. At 9:30, the guests and hosts parted happily.

Mr. Liang Yansun's Second Anniversary Memorial Meeting Held at Baoben Hall Yesterday 139

Yesterday (the 9th) was the second anniversary of Mr. Liang Yansun's death. Relatives and friends in Shanghai held a memorial meeting at Baoben Hall on Changsha Road. More than two hundred people attended, including Ye Yuhu, Lu Jianquan, Qian Xinzhi, Wu Daquan, Hu Bijiang, Feng Gengguang, Liu Tiecheng, Huang Renzhi, Lin Xisheng, Lu Dingkui, Zhang Mingzhen, Hu Mengjia, Li Fuhou, Chen Zheqing, Wang Zijian, and aided students. Mr. Liang's calligraphy and paintings, foundation documents, student achievements, etc. were displayed in the venue. The most precious of these were two handwritten letters from Mr. Liang Rengong inviting Mr. Liang to Tianjin to discuss national affairs before the brewing of the Hongxian monarchy, and the communication issued by the Reuters telegram in Tokyo at that time regarding Mr. Liang's opposition to the monarchy (this communication was translated and presented to Yuan Shikai by Zhengzhuan Hall, and Yuan personally wrote "Sent to Mr. Liang for review"). There were also documents on handling foreign affairs, and the first railway tickets issued in our country, etc. The meeting was announced to be open, and then Mr. Ye Yuhu was publicly elected as the chairman. Flowers were offered to Mr. Liang's portrait and rituals were performed as usual. After the ceremony, Lu Jianquan, recommended by the Academic Scholarship Committee, reported on the receipt and payment of the scholarship fund, stating briefly that the scholarship fund has now purchased and stored 210,000 yuan in government bonds and that more than 5,100 yuan was spent on subsidies this year. Then, Mr. Lin Xisheng, recommended by the Academic Scholarship Committee, reported on the achievements of the subsidized students. There are currently fifteen students receiving scholarships, and their average grades are all above 80 points. The schools where the subsidized students are enrolled are Tianjin Nankai, Beijing Normal, Shanghai Jiaotong, Nanjing Jinling, Guangzhou Lingnan, and Guangxi University, etc. Then, Mr. Ye Yuhu, recommended by the Editorial Committee of the Collection of Literary Works, reported on the progress of editing the Collection of Literary Works, briefly stating that at the beginning of editing the Collection of Literary Works, a letter was sent to solicit Mr. Liang's life, words, deeds, and deeds, but not much was obtained. All rely on the collection of all parties. Now the chronology has been compiled to 1917. After 1918, it has also begun. It was originally intended to be completed by the end of this year, but I dare not say that there is certainty. I hope that the colleagues present will continue to work hard to collect and supply so that human and financial resources will not be wasted and we can see its success as soon as possible. After the report, there was a recording of Mr. Liang's economic speech in 1924, which was to develop the national economy and prepare six tools. In the speech, he repeatedly mentioned the three northeastern provinces, which meant that Mr. Liang was aware of the neighbor's economic invasion of the northeastern provinces at the time of the speech. After the playback, Mr. Zhang Jianquan, Mr. Hu Yuantan, and others spoke in succession, saying that Mr. Liang's life-long dedication and contribution to the country, society, economy, and education can be seen from today's displayed documents, recordings, and scholarship undertakings after his death. They expressed their deep admiration. After the meeting, the Academic Scholarship Committee was held to discuss various important matters this year.

New Merchants in Huai Salt Region Request Equal Treatment from Five Banks: Continued Lending While Avoiding Monopoly by Old Merchants 140

The Xin Sheng News Agency reports: Since the implementation of the rotational sales system for salt from the Huaibei region sold in Bangbu and along the Wan River, the method has been quite appropriate. However, banks generally do not provide tax loans to new merchants, requiring them to raise their own tax funds. Additionally, they do not offer loans against salt when it arrives, leading to financial difficulties. Recently, a group of new merchants, including Li Cheng and others, wrote to the Shanghai headquarters of various banks, outlining their concerns: "Bangbu is the sole authorized port for the sale of Huai salt, and borrowing from banks against arriving salt is the only way for merchants to manage their finances. This system has been convenient for many years. Recently, your banks have ceased offering tax loans and salt-backed loans to new merchants trading in Bangbu, while continuing to provide loans and ample funds to the existing thirty-odd merchants. We find several aspects of this inexplicable and respectfully request clarification.

We understand that your bank's differential treatment of new and old merchants may be due to existing tax agreements. However, these new merchants are transporting salt in accordance with regulations and have obtained approval from the government authorities beforehand. The new tax salt must be sold in order of arrival and through a rotational system after the existing eighty-nine trainloads have been cleared. This demonstrates the government's care in protecting bank loans and safeguarding the capital of the existing merchants. Therefore, there is no possibility of the new merchants disrupting the port sales or hindering bank lending. Yet your banks discriminate against the new merchants' salt by refusing to provide either tax loans or salt-backed loans. This is inexplicable.

Perhaps your bank believes that the creditworthiness of new merchants is inferior to that of old merchants, making you unwilling to provide tax loans. While this might be understandable, the salt has already arrived, and each bag costs eleven yuan. The quality and weight have been inspected and certified by the government, making it indistinguishable from the salt of established merchants. Yet we cannot even obtain loans at a discounted rate. This is also inexplicable.

Or perhaps your bank is currently pursuing a policy of tightening credit, with set quotas for total lending, and thus temporarily refusing to provide loans. However, you continue to provide ample new tax funds to the old merchants, disguising it as '拼裝' (piecing together) or '凑車' (grouping cars). According to railway regulations, a full carload of fifteen tons or more is sufficient for joint transportation. Even if it requires piecing together, several dozen to several hundred '担' (a unit of weight) should be enough. Why then are you piecing together several thousand '担'? This is the third inexplicable matter.

We aim to promote the sale of salt produced in our respective regions, and therefore have no choice but to trade in Bangbu. However, our capital is limited, allowing us to transport only tens or hundreds of tons at a time. This approach, with each merchant transporting smaller quantities, can alleviate difficulties and reduce the problem of excessive inventory at the port. These are our humble views.

Regarding whether your banks provide tax loans, you have your own policies, and we are not in a position to comment. However, we hope that all salt arriving at the port will be treated equally and that you will continue to provide loans as usual. This would be in line with your bank's duty to regulate social finance and support small businesses, while avoiding the creation of a monopolistic situation. Therefore, we dare to present our concerns and respectfully request a clear explanation. We await your response with great anticipation."

Respectfully submitted to: Zhang, General Manager of the Bank of China; Chen, General Manager of the Shanghai Bank; Tang, General Manager of the Bank of Communications; Xu, General Manager of the Jiangsu Bank; and Xu, General Manager of the Zhejiang Industrial Bank.

By: Li Yongxing, Qiao Fusheng Gong, Ji Yuan An Salt Firm, and twenty-six other firms.

County Administration Expert Wang Guanxian Returns from the United States 141

Mr. Wang Guanxian, a native of Jiangsu, is a graduate of the former National Southeast University. In the 17th year [of the Republic], he passed the Jiangsu Province exam for county magistrates and served as magistrate in Baoying, Funing, and Gaochun counties, among others, with outstanding achievements. He also devoted his spare time to writing and research, offering insightful analyses and suggestions for improving county administration. After resigning from his post two years ago, he went to the United States to specialize in local administration. He obtained a Master of Arts degree in political science from the University of Michigan in one year, with excellent grades. He was highly praised by Professor Ralph, a renowned expert in municipal administration in the United States. We have learned that Mr. Wang returned to China yesterday. He stated that given the increasingly precarious state of the nation in recent years, genuine reform of local politics is necessary to unlock the full potential of the entire political system. He intends to publish a comprehensive article outlining his views for consideration by the authorities.

Summary of the Jisheng Association's Spring Relief Efforts in Liyang 142

The China Jisheng Association notes that last year's drought was exceptionally severe, and the disaster victims are in dire need of assistance. As the period between harvests approaches, the spring relief efforts in Yixing, Jiangsu Province, have been jointly organized with the China and Foreign Relief Association and are currently underway. The situation in Liyang is particularly dire, and representatives from the county have repeatedly come to Shanghai urgently requesting relief. The association, in consultation with the China and Foreign Relief Association, has jointly organized relief efforts and appointed Mr. Li Yunmen as the director. He, along with relief workers, is scheduled to travel to Liyang on the 9th of this month to investigate and implement spring relief measures. However, with the scale of the disaster being vast and funds being limited, the efforts are akin to a drop in the bucket. How much relief can the disaster victims receive? It is hoped that charitable individuals at home and abroad will act with compassion and generously donate to save lives, for saving a life is more meritorious than building a seven-story pagoda. The merit is truly immeasurable.

Huining Fellow-Provincials Association Requests Duty-Free Rice for Famine Relief 143

The Huining Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai learned that the central government had issued permits for 100,000 "石" (a unit of dry volume) of duty-free foreign rice for Anhui province, to be distributed by the provincial disaster relief committee to the affected counties. Upon hearing this news, the association immediately telegraphed the provincial capital on the 30th of last month to request permits to aid the famine in the twelve counties formerly under the jurisdiction of Huizhou and Ningguo. The association has now received a telegram from the provincial disaster relief committee stating that the duty-free permits have already been allocated: Shexian, Yixian, Jixi, and Qimen counties in Huizhou each received 2,000 "石," and Xiuning and Wuyuan each received 4,000 "石." Xuancheng, Nanling, Ningguo, Jingxian, Jingde, and Taiping counties in Ningguo each received 2,000 "石." The association has been requested to inform the respective county governments to contact them for permits. It is reported that the association has already telegraphed the county governments to prepare official documents and collect them directly from the provincial disaster relief committee.

Austrian Female Ice Skating Expert Arrives in Shanghai 144

The Continental Daily News reports that Ms. White Jack, a 22-year-old Austrian ice skating expert, recently accepted an invitation from the Japan Ice Skating Association to perform in Tokyo several times. After staying in Japan for two months, she is now passing through Shanghai on her way back to her home country. Ms. Jack amazed Europe with her ice skating skills at the age of eleven. She won the silver medal in the ice skating competition at the Olympic Games in both 1928 and 1932. After returning home, she plans to train diligently, hoping to win the women's ice skating championship at the next Olympic Games. Ms. Jack expressed her surprise that Shanghai, a city as prosperous as it is, does not have a single ice skating rink. She also noted that since the last Olympic Games, there has been a significant increase in the number of men and women learning to ice skate in Japan, and their progress has been rapid. Tokyo now has three ice skating rinks, one of which is as large as the Lake Placid ice skating rink in the United States. Osaka and other major cities each have at least one ice skating rink.

The resolution was passed. Industrial and commercial firms in Zhabei that need credit loans can register between 1:00 PM and 5:00 PM daily. The resolution was passed. The resolution was passed. (6) No registration fees will be charged to those who register for industrial and commercial credit loans. All regular expenses of the meeting will be borne by the committee members. The resolution was passed. (7) The Zhabei Chamber of Commerce Relief Committee should establish departments for social, general affairs, organization, investigation, economics, and publicity. Each department will have seven members, who will also serve on the executive committee. The resolution was passed. The meeting adjourned.

General Manager of Electric Power Company McCaw Retires and Returns Home 146

Mr. McCaw, the general manager of the Shanghai Electric Power Company, is a Scotsman from Britain who has been engaged in business in the Far East, in China and Japan, for 35 years. Since arriving in Shanghai in 1914, he has been affiliated with the Electricity Department of the Municipal Council. When the department was reorganized into the Electric Power Company, Mr. McCaw was appointed as the general manager, a position he has held for 21 years. He is now retiring from the company due to old age and physical decline. He left Shanghai yesterday with his family aboard the Empress of Asia for a long vacation in his home country, where he will enjoy his remaining years.

Dinghai Fellow-Provincials Association to Rebuild Hall and Relocate Charity House: Fellow-Provincials Registry First 147

On December 9th of last year, the Dinghai Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai held a memorial service for Mr. He Caitang at the Dinghai Hall on Pingjili Road. Approximately several hundred people attended. Taking advantage of the gathering, they discussed various issues such as renovating the hall, merging the fellow-provincials association, and relocating the Shanzhang Charity House. Mr. Chen Yiting spoke first, stating that the hall had been established for over 30 years and needed repairs costing approximately 20,000 yuan. The current fund is approximately 40,000 yuan. If this fund is used for repairs, the fund will be reduced, and the income will also decrease, which may not be sufficient for future expenses. He suggested rebuilding the hall into a three- or four-story Western-style building, adding rental housing on both sides, and relocating the fellow-provincials association to the hall for office space. This would both increase the usable space and generate more income, which would be a win-win situation. Mr. Pan Shanglin then spoke, stating that the Shanzhang Charity House in Rihuigang has been ordered to relocate within three years. The area is becoming more prosperous, and land prices are also rising. He suggested converting the land into rental housing, and the rental income would be the Charity House's regular expenses. He suggested purchasing 50 "亩" (a unit of area) of land at a low price in or near the Hongkou Zhibei or Beixinjing area and building a charity house there. This land purchase would be funded by donations from fellow-provincials, whether it be one "亩", half a "亩", or a quarter of a "亩." The idea is to gather contributions together. There are tens of thousands of fellow-provincials in Shanghai, surely they have the ability to contribute more than 50 "亩." As long as they are enthusiastic, there will surely be success. Mr. Chen Dafang then spoke, stating that the fellow-provincials present should know how many fellow-provincials there are in Shanghai, and even more importantly, how many poor and unemployed fellow-provincials there are. To know these numbers, the fellow-provincials association must first register the population. The method would be to set up group leaders in each district, who would register the residents together with the staff of the fellow-provincials association. If honest and reliable unemployed individuals are found, the fellow-provincials association can find ways to introduce them or send them back to their hometown to prevent them from wandering in other places. On the other hand, the small-to-middle-class families can do their part for the hall. Many hands make light work. The renovation of the hall and the relocation of the charity house can both arise from the registration. Subsequently, Mr. Xu Tingzuo and Mr. Qian Derun made similar supplementary speeches. Liu Hongsheng, Xu Tingzuo, Qian Derun, Chen Yiting, and Pan Shanglin were nominated as members of the preparatory committee. It has been reported that the Dinghai Fellow-Provincials Association is starting with the registration process and gradually implementing the above points.

Waiter at China Restaurant Sues for Divorce 151

Lin Zhisong, a native of Ningbo, is currently working as a waiter at the China Restaurant. In the 19th year [of the Republic], he married his fellow-provincial woman Qiu Axiu (26 years old) through a matchmaker. They rented a house at No. 65 Ruicing Lane, East Jiaxing Road.
