Free Talk

Year of Old Books 201

— Wei Shu

Dear readers! Last year, the reading class generally recognized as the year of magazines. What will this year become? Looking at the three-month process in the publishing industry, I will try to create a name for you! "Year of Old Books."

On the one hand, booksellers are inheriting the sentiments of the magazine year, blindly competing in the market, and specialized intermediaries who rely on the sales of magazines have also emerged. On the other hand, they are stopping the publication of new books and only using the sale and reprinting of old books to decorate the facade. Books and books that were placed under real, historical evaluation are now rampant. This is precisely because "books" are a part of the enterprise and are governed by the natural law of periodic panic.

"Year of Old Books," as the name suggests, is old books. At present, more than half of the bookstores that specialize in publishing new books are holding price reductions and selling slightly soiled and damaged books at the lowest price. Booksellers watch blankly during the good market conditions, the "books" that were frantically published due to competition are piled up in large quantities, and they have to painfully cut prices to convert them into currency.

The other object of the "Year of Old Books," in terms of quality, is the competition of old and outdated books. One bookstore publishes the Collected Works of Yuan Zhonglang, and another bookstore publishes the Complete Works of Yuan Zhonglang. The reprinting competition between the Twenty-Five Histories and the Twenty-Six Histories, which led to litigation, etc., are the best examples that can be picked up at hand. Recently, a bookstore is calling for a literary system that compiles the new literary trends of the first ten years, which is a more clever move. Because reprinting old books is definitely less costly, at least there is no need to pay royalties; and the book price can be arbitrarily raised, and there is no danger of suffering any danger. However, because of the vastness of the pages and the high pricing, the book industry has been separated from the general reading class, and there is a trend to become a kind of decoration. In short, the rise of old books, on the one hand, is the decline of people engaged in the work of "books"; on the other hand, it is because the ability to purchase books is weak, and at the same time, there is no way to obtain books, which makes the reader class decline with wisdom. This fact is enough to cause cultural stagnation and decline, which is the most obvious thing.

Enlightenment 202

— Another Realm

Speaking of enlightenment, Christianity is probably no match for Buddhism and Taoism. The reason why religion is religion is that making people understand is an important element. Without enlightenment, there will be no infatuation, and there will be no faith. Religion cannot exist. "Oh, I see!" This is the "enlightenment" that is often encountered in ordinary life, but ordinary people cannot always be enlightened after one enlightenment. Although religious people are constantly reminding you: "Turning back is the shore," there are very few who can truly change their ways from then on. There are still those who jump into the Huangpu River for the second time.

Since there have been humans on Earth, religion has existed. The current religions generally advocate peace, but primitive religions were not like this. This change is, in my opinion, a major progress in the history of religion. Why is Islam not as powerful as Christianity? The steel knife that Muhammad held in his hand is very important. It is impossible to hold people's hearts by force, even if they can "eat," they will not truly wholeheartedly become your believers. It is more clever than him, but he still cannot get rid of "eating." Once everything comes to eating, there will always be choruses.

Then, doesn't all "enlightenment" have to start from "eating"? Not necessarily. There are plenty of people in the world who are enlightened because they have hit a wall when they eat. For example, Sakyamuni of Buddhism became enlightened because he was too full, but such examples are rare. Most of the "enlightenment" is for hunger. Only when the stomach is hungry can there be a real feeling of "enlightenment." At this time, "enlightenment" cannot be controlled by Muhammad, who holds a steel knife. The rebellions in history can be said to be the greatest expression of "enlightenment."

Religious people often say "this person is enlightened," which is equivalent to saying "this person is hungry." Therefore, the secular name for believers is "eating religion," which can be said to be the most thorough annotation. A sick person does not avoid seeing a doctor. I think religious people should also agree with this. Therefore, in summary, the root of "enlightenment" is "hunger." It develops in two directions: one is worldly, that is, believers; the other is worldly, that is, revolutionaries. Sakyamuni can be said to be the supreme believer of enlightenment. To put it bluntly, he is just a perverted "enlightenment."

On "Scholars Despise Each Other" (2) 203

— Cao Juren

Around the fifth century AD, Southern literati paid special attention to the application of tones in literature. The Biography of Lu Jue in the History of the Southern Dynasties says: "During the Yongming period, writing was popular, and Shen Yue of Wuxing, Xie Tiao of Chenjun, and Wang Rong of Langya promoted each other in terms of temperament. Zhou Yong of Runan was good at recognizing sounds and rhymes. Yue and other articles all used palace sounds: using the four tones of level, rising, departing, and entering, to create rhymes, there are flat heads, upward tails, wasp waists, and crane knees. Among the five characters, the sounds and rhymes are all different: within two sentences, the notes of the scale are different; they cannot be increased or decreased, and the world calls it the Yongming style." Shen Yue believed that "since Ling Jun, there have been many generations, although the literary style has been slightly refined, this secret has not been seen. As for high words and wonderful sentences, they are all secretly in harmony with reason, not from thought." (On the Biography of Xie Lingyun in the Book of Song) He believed that "since ancient times, poets, how could they not know the difference between palace and feather, and the difference between business and sign; although they know the difference between the five tones, they do not know much about the differences and changes among them. Therefore, my humble opinion is that this secret has not been seen. Based on this, we know that the literati of the previous generations did not realize this point. If the tones and rhymes of articles are the same as the sounds and tunes of strings and pipes, then beauty and ugliness cannot be completely contradictory; it is like Ziye playing music, how can there be any intermittent and out-of-tune sounds? Comparing Luoshen to Chen Si's other odes is like a different work. Therefore, we know that when the heavenly machine is turned on, the rhythm will be adjusted automatically, and when the six emotions are stagnant, the tone will be dissonant." (Reply to Lu Jue's letter) And Zhong Rong, who was opposed to him, put forward another proposition: "In the past, Cao and Liu were almost the saints of literature, and Lu and Xie were the talents of the second style, who were keen on research and thinking. For thousands of years, they have never heard of the distinction between palace and business, and the theory of the four tones. Or some say that the former talents accidentally did not see it, how could it be? Let me try to say it: In ancient times, poems and hymns were all covered with gold and bamboo, so they could not be harmonized without tuning the five tones... Now that they are not covered with pipes and strings, why should they take the sound and rhythm? ... Wang Yuanchang created its head, and Xie Tiao and Shen Yue promoted its waves. The three sages may be the sons and grandsons of noble families, and they had literary debate since childhood. Therefore, the scholars admired it and tried to be precise, accumulating subtle details and specializing in mutual trampling. Therefore, they made the text restrained and hurt its true beauty. I think the literary system must be recited and read, and it must not be jerky. But if it is clear and smooth, and the tone is smooth, it is enough. As for the level, rising, departing, and entering, I am sick and cannot do it; the wasp waist and crane knees are already available in the neighborhoods." (Preface to the Book of Poetry) They only had such differences in opinion due to their partial attachment to literary skills, which led to endless attacks, which is also a phase of scholars despising each other.

Tolstoy said: "The artists of various schools slander and smear each other, just like the religious people of various schools. Look at the artists of various schools now, people of one school criticize people of another school: for example, in poetry, the old Romantic school excludes the Byronic school and the decadent school; the Byronic school excludes the Romantic school and the decadent school; the decadent school excludes the previous schools and the Symbolist school; the Symbolist school excludes the previous schools and the Magog school, and the Magog school excludes the above schools... The same is true in novels, dramas, paintings, and music." (On Art) Therefore, in Tolstoy's view of art, Shakespeare's plays cannot occupy any position. Even if we look at the opinions of poets on poetry in the Ming and Qing dynasties, there is the same tendency to diverge. Li Mengyang "advocated that writing must be from the Qin and Han dynasties, and poetry must be from the prosperous Tang dynasty, and those who are not are not allowed to speak." (Biography of Li in the History of Ming) He attacked Song poetry, saying that "poetry to the Tang dynasty, the ancient tune is dead. However, since the Tang dynasty, the tune can be sung, and the higher ones can still be covered with pipes and strings. The people of the Song dynasty focus on reason and not on tune, so the Tang tune is also dead. Huang (Tingjian) and Chen (Shidao) learn from Du Fu and are called masters; now their words are difficult and unfloral, like entering a temple and sitting on a mud and wood skeleton, even if the crown and clothes are the same as people, can they be called people?" (Preface to Mengyang's Can Yin) And the Temperament School attacked He and Li's theory of style, and the rhetoric was equally sharp. Yuan Zhonglang said: "Why must poetry be from the Tang dynasty, and why must it be early and prosperous? It is necessary to use those that come from temperament as true poetry. Temperament resides in the heart and dwells in the environment. When the environment is accidentally touched, the heart can capture it; what the heart wants to spit out, the wrist can transport it. ... Use the heart to capture the environment, and use the wrist to transport the heart, then temperament will be fully expressed; this is called true poetry, and why must it be from the Tang dynasty, and why must the early and prosperous be complacent?" Yuan Zicai said: "Yang Chengzhai said: 'People with low talent and clumsiness like to talk about style, but they do not understand interest, why? Style is an empty shelf, and it is easy to describe the tune, but interest specializes in writing temperament, which cannot be done without genius.' ... You must know that there is style and rhythm if there is temperament, and rhythm is not outside of temperament. Half of the three hundred poems are about working people and bereaved women, who express their feelings casually. Who makes the style? Who makes the rhythm? Can those who talk about style today go beyond their scope?" (Volume 1 of Suiyuan Poetry Talks) The style theory and the temperament theory are the two major schools of poetry theory, and with the addition of Wang Yuyang's charm theory, they are divided into three parts.

Childhood 204

— Chi Xia

When I see a group of lively children jumping around on the ground, I immediately recall my own lost childhood. The impressions are so vague yet so clear – as vague as a dream I had, yet as clear as something I personally experienced.

More than twenty years ago, I too was as lively and happy as these little angels! Like a carefree little bird, flying in the open sky. When pain came, I would cry aloud; if I encountered unexpected joy, I would laugh endlessly. Even a small matter like watching a group of ants carrying things in a pile of rocks could occupy my absorbed attention for an hour or two. Not only did I find it interesting myself, but I would sometimes insist on dragging neighboring children to watch with me. When we were tired of watching and playing, we would pick up stones to help the defeated ones fight back against the victors. Then everyone would burst into laughter. Each person's face, bearing a compassionate envy, would reveal a triumphant benevolence. How honest are the hearts of children! If one were to say that there is such a thing as helping the weak and suppressing the strong in this world, then it can only be found in the souls of the young.

Sometimes, among us children, we would fall out over a small matter. However, after a short while, we would tacitly forget the minor rift immediately, and become as close as our own siblings. I remember once, because a friend insisted on helping the red ants invade the black ants' food supply, and I, who had always disliked the red ones, expressed my disagreement. The barbaric friend immediately started hitting me, and naturally, I fought back. For an entire day, we didn't speak to each other. But the next day, we made up again, forgetting the previous day's small rift completely. The hearts of children are flawless. Their external appearance and internal feelings can only reveal the same color. It's not like adults who can still smile at people even when they are angry!

Although children can be naughty, they have no worries or calculations. Their minds are truly as pure as blank paper. No color can stain their firm and clean hearts. When they make a fuss, it's to develop their childish nature, to naturally stretch their muscles and bones. If the world of mankind could always remain in its childhood, I think a more peaceful and tranquil society could certainly be realized.

Time flows like water. The golden age of childhood has actually slipped away in the history of my life. When I see those little angels jumping around so lively, a feeling of envy arises from the bottom of my heart. Ten years from now, they will be like us, walking the path of adulthood. At that time, this momentary joy will only be enough to provide endless memories for the future.

Dusk 205

— Luo Fang

The afterglow of the setting sun gradually ceases to ripple,

The sky changes from azure to ashen gray;

A cool evening breeze gently flows into my empty chest,

I vaguely feel a sense of loss,

Carrying a restless heart, I wander aimlessly down the street,

Gazing at the shadows of the plane trees slowly moving on the wall,

Gradually dimming and disappearing.

The fragrance of wheat and broad beans floats in the air,

A small patch of mud in front of the courtyard releases the breath of spring;

I breathe deeply,

Feeling an unbearable thirst,

Carrying a leaden heart, I wander aimlessly down the street,

Gazing at wild geese flying across the ashen gray sky,

Gradually becoming smaller and disappearing.

A thin layer of mist covers the surroundings,

All scenery, blurred, loses its vitality,

The streets are filled with noise and coal smoke;

I hold down the beating in my heart, listening carefully

To the long, drawn-out whistle of a distant train,

The muscles in my limbs tremble slightly,

Vaguely imagining from the South Sea and the Northern Lands,

A seed of hope flying in.

I laugh wildly in front of everyone,

I weep towards the ashen gray sky;

But, fatigue permeates my whole body,

Loneliness is like a vast black curtain hanging before my eyes,

I can only wander aimlessly on the endless streets,

Praying to grasp something,

To stir up excitement and intoxication, in a moment

Forgetting the sorrow of my soul.

Mr. Juqing (11) 206

— Ke Ling

He deliberately watched Shen Qingzhong's every move. The moment he found a fault, he would immediately sink his gaunt face and shout a single word at Shen Qingzhong in a heavy voice:

"Come!"

Shen Qingzhong was just about to slip a paper ring onto the braid tie of a classmate who was copying a book nearby, when he suddenly heard the teacher's roar. He hastily retracted his hand, and turned around to be met by Mr. Juqing's pair of sunken and terribly wide eyes. He ran up to him, bewildered.

Mr. Juqing did not say a word. His right hand grabbed the thick "discipline ruler" on the table, his left hand grabbed Shen Qingzhong's small hand and pressed it against the corner of the table. He concentrated all of his pent-up anger and resentment onto the "discipline ruler" in his right hand. The whole classroom was silent, only the crisp sound of the bamboo piece hitting flesh could be heard –

Crack, crack, crack, crack…

More than a dozen times in a row, the small palm was already red. Mr. Juqing waved his hand, and Shen Qingzhong quickly returned to his seat, laid down on his desk, and burst into tears.

This crying gave Mr. Juqing a bone-deep satisfaction.

Unexpectedly, this corporal punishment education had not yet achieved its intended effect. That evening, a tall woman with a square face came, introduced herself as Shen Qingzhong's mother, and said to Mr. Juqing with a somewhat cold expression:

"Our Qingzhong is still young. Studying is just a matter for the study room. This child is also born thin and frail. At home, we rarely even raise our voices to him; so I hope that the teacher will not beat him like this in the future. Now the child's hand is swollen like a crab shell."

Toward this woman who completely lacked etiquette, Mr. Juqing was almost about to jump up in anger; but for some reason, he had no courage at all. He stood there dumbfounded for a long time, unable to think of even a suitable reply. It was Mr. Juqing's wife who squinted her eyes and said many kind words from the side, before this woman finally left in a leisurely manner.

Because of this small disturbance, Mr. Juqing's bright mood turned gloomy again. Moreover, he had a more profound feeling of "the decline of the teaching profession."

Because of this, he was depressed for several days again.

Not long after, just as Mr. Juqing's troubles had somewhat subsided, rumors spread like wind and brought new worries. An unexpected storm stirred on the calm lake.

This was a change that was even more impossible to deal with and more difficult to cope with than the "student conduct" issue. It was said that the district elementary school had learned that the private tutors were taking advantage of their turmoil to fish in troubled waters and pull in students from the school. Now they had decided on a way to deal with it and were going to take revenge.

Therefore, carrying a heavy heart, he heard all sorts of different news morning and evening.

One piece of news said that the district elementary school had already submitted an official letter to the county, and the education bureau would soon send personnel to the countryside to ban private schools.

Page 17

Finance: Central Bank Aggressively Sells Shillings, Bullion's Upward Momentum Weak, Exchange Rate Improves by One and a Half Yuan 207

The gold market remained indecisive yesterday, with unstable sentiment. Although there was a rebound in the middle, the upward trend was only temporary. The Central Bank and the Bank of China aggressively sold foreign exchange, stirring up selling pressure. Despite the negative news, there was still a downward trend. Sassoon covered short positions, ultimately stabilizing the market. In the early morning, the overseas silver market rose slightly in both the UK and the US. The Montreal forward silver market rose slightly, and exchange rates all contracted. London spot gold rose by ten pence. Reports indicated that the Ministry of Finance had drafted a three-article outline on unifying the right to issue banknotes under the Central Bank, which slightly moved market sentiment. Preparatory trading opened in the off-exchange market, immediately rising to 67.8 yuan. Although there was supply, the Central Bank's listed exchange rates revealed that the British rate was flat and the US rate contracted. The customs gold unit rose by one fen, and the bullion standard price rose to 905.3 yuan, and then to over 9 yuan. After opening, the sentiment seemed to rebound, and buyers took advantage of the opportunity, soon breaking through the 70 yuan mark and gradually rising. Banks seized the opportunity to sell high. The exchange market should have been consistent, but after rising, it gradually retreated to within 70 yuan. The Hongkong and Shanghai Banking Corporation (HSBC) listed its exchange rates, with the British rate flat and the US rate contracting by 0.0625. At this time, short sellers were still covering and mostly hovering. The Central Bank suddenly offered to sell, and the situation remained difficult to improve. Later, a negative news report from the Associated Press indicated that the Bank of China was aggressively selling, and the internal shilling market turned strong. Buyers were helpless, and selling pressure rose again, repeatedly weakening the market and causing frequent declines. — (Yang Xieli)

Passivity, inaction, fear of trouble, clearly declining but always interpreting it as "detached"; recklessly rushing, stirring up waves without wind, clearly being unruly but always thinking of it as "striving hard." Alas! What value is there in such "detachment" and "struggle"!

The more effort one puts into doing things, the more likely one is to encounter bad luck; because the more effort one puts in, the greater the responsibility one bears, and effort does not necessarily lead to success. Once there is failure, the blame will be severe.

Illegitimate Child 224

— Zhou Xian

It was a warm spring morning, with a gentle breeze carrying the sounds of a newborn baby's cries. The cries were so powerful and full of rhythm.

Outside the door, there was a commotion of voices, all talking about an abandoned illegitimate child left under the overpass in the alley. Sure enough, under the overpass, on a pile of straw, lay a small child, wrapped in pink velvet and tied with a floral ribbon. His hands and feet were powerfully extending and contracting, as if preparing to fight in this world. Tears welled up in the corners of his eyes, and his mouth opened in constant "wah wah" cries, as if lamenting the misfortune of his life, the misfortune of being an abandoned illegitimate child.

A large crowd had gathered to watch, some in surprise, some in sighs, some in daze, and some laughing with their mouths wide open. But although there were so many people watching! And the child was crying with such vigor, yet not one had the courage to even touch him, as if the child were bringing impurity into this world. Those watching the spectacle were all gossiping about which family's scandalous daughter had engaged in such shameless behavior, resulting in this... nuisance.

Finally, an old Buddhist woman squeezed out from the crowd. She chanted Buddha's name and picked up the child. Upon unwrapping him, she discovered that he was indeed a baby boy, still stained with unwashed blood. Tucked in front of his chest were two five-yuan bills and a letter begging someone to raise him.

The old woman chanted Buddha's name a few times, tucked the bills into her pocket, hired a rickshaw, and sent the illegitimate child to the orphanage.

Hotel 225

— Ba Ling

Stepping into a hotel is a rare event for me. If I calculate it, I probably don't go more than three or four times a year, right?

It was probably in the middle of last month! I agreed to meet a friend and stepped into a small hotel in the front street of the ×× Temple in S City. The time was around 7:00 PM, just when the lanterns in S City's Chinese area were brightly lit.

There were a total of four or five people in our group. We chose a relatively quiet table to sit down at. Naturally, the waiters were very attentive in serving us! We ordered some wine and a few dishes, and then we started drinking heartily. At that moment, I personally felt that all of life's pain and sorrow could only be relieved by drinking. No wonder most poets and writers are happy to be close to this stuff.

While eating, we talked about everything from national affairs to social trivia, and from social trivia to personal anecdotes. Everyone spoke frankly and without restraint. I really wondered if there was any hypocrisy or pretense in the world? I thought to myself, understandingly.

The thing that made me most dissatisfied in the hotel was the noise of the drinkers. Some were talking loudly and expressing their frustrations at not being recognized for their talent. Others were drinking silently, seemingly using alcohol to drown their sorrows. The waiters were running around serving the drinkers, looking very busy. I observed everything in the hotel and realized that this was a small society, a small world. Look: the noise and clamor in the hotel brings together the attitudes displayed by all kinds of people and classes in society. Isn't this a microcosm of society?

"Alas. I didn't expect this small hotel to be a place for studying social problems," I thought silently as I returned.

Chapter Eleven: Nightly Conversations of a Sad Life, Dreams of Footprints Scattered in the Wind and Rain, Too Much Deception

Zhiqian was stunned upon hearing these words. He thought to himself that he always wanted to save this poor girl. But no matter how he ran around, she could never escape the grasp of these demons. Matchmaking, but for whom? He pondered this, hesitating for several minutes, but when he came to his senses, the tea server who had spoken was already far away. Zhiqian regretted not asking the tea server more clearly who wanted this girl. He pondered for a while, and then two gusts of wind blew in, bringing the rain directly into the doorway. The dampness on his face made him shiver, and he had no choice but to return to his room. Behind his room was a window that faced the backyard. He was paying attention to the matchmaking for Huanhua, so he paced back and forth in the room, constantly looking out the back window. After about half an hour, Hu Xiaojiao arrived with an umbrella and a smile on his face. Judging by the situation, there was some hope of success in the matchmaking. He should have gone out to stop her and ask what was going on. But then he thought about how he had introduced a maid for Zhu Yueying yesterday, and the matter had not been settled, so people might be suspicious. He paced, thinking it over. But by the time he had finished thinking it over, Sister Hu had already gone to Jia Duocai's place. Not long after, Sister Hu returned. The wind was blowing hard, and she could not hold the umbrella steady. She kept the umbrella half-closed, holding it over her head, and quickly walked towards the back door. The wind was strong, so the rain was naturally slanting, wetting a lot of her clothes. However, she did not mind and walked away calmly. (178)

Small Statistics 230

— (Long Sheng)

A fingernail grows one thirty-second of an inch per week, or a little over one and a half inches per year. Growth is faster in summer than in winter. The middle fingernail grows fastest, and the thumb slowest. Fingernails on the right hand grow faster than those on the left, and they grow completely in about four and a half months. For example, a seventy-year-old person has 186 new sets of fingernails. At half an inch per time, each finger grows seven feet and nine inches, for a total of seventy-seven and a half feet for ten fingers.

The Book of Songs has 39,124 characters, the Book of Documents has 25,700 characters, the Rites of Zhou has 45,806 characters, the Record of Rites has 99,020 characters, the Book of Changes has 24,107 characters, the Analects has 12,700 characters, the Mencius has 34,085 characters, the Classic of Filial Piety has 1,903 characters, the Zuo Commentary on the Spring and Autumn Annals has 200,135 characters, the Book of Etiquette and Ceremonial has 56,624 characters, the Gongyang Commentary has 44,015 characters, and the Guliang Commentary has 41,512 characters, for a total of 626,706 characters. Reading 500 characters per day, with weekly holidays, can be completed in four years.

Short Story

Escape 231

— Pan Zhaogan

The spring rain fell continuously, making the weather extremely cold. The dim and gloomy sky was filled with countless gray-black rain clouds. Fine rain fell in slanting lines, wetting a dry dirt road.

"Sir, Madam, save, save a poor child like me!"

The sound came closer and closer. After a few minutes, a small child with a dark face and a hungry expression stumbled through the wind and rain.

"Old man, alms, alms!" At this time, the child had walked from the rain to the entrance of the Wang family's house and was pleading with the gatekeeper, trembling slightly.

"Get out of here! Who cares about your business so early in the morning." As he spoke, his face turned fierce.

"Old man, I haven't eaten for three days! Have some compassion, please give me some alms!"

"Who told you not to eat for three days? You hateful beggar, are you not leaving?" The old man's voice was stern, showing that he was angry.

The child knew that he would not get any money, so he had to leave. But a group of dogs behind him rushed up, roaring and running, almost catching the child. The child was knocked down on a muddy road, and the dogs sniffed around him for a while, singing a song of victory and returning.

When he woke up, his clothes were soaked through with rain, his stomach was extremely hungry, and it hurt very badly. Pointless sobbing only increased his hunger. When he stood up, he felt completely weak. An old woman came back from the market carrying a vegetable basket.

"Old woman, save me!" the child pleaded vaguely.

"Poor child, why are you walking in the rain? Go and sit at the entrance of the Wang family's house over there for a while!" The old woman was very compassionate and walked forward with the child's hand.

"Old woman, I... I won't go over there... there are scary... dogs over there!"

"Poor child, then go to my house! How old are you?"

"Old woman, eleven years old."

As he spoke, he reached the entrance of the old woman's house. The child was afraid and did not dare to go in.

"It's okay, come in!" the old woman said kindly. The child followed her in, and she told him to stand outside. She went in and brought out a bowl of cold rice, giving it to the child to eat.

The child quickly finished the rice, his eyes wide and staring blankly.

"Child, do you have parents?"

"Old woman, my father died long ago. Last year, my mother sold me to the city, to a place called the Quanwang Temple..." The child stopped abruptly when he said this, and a boundless terror appeared on his face again.

"Poor child, speak freely, it doesn't matter now! Why did you become like this?"

"Old woman, I... I..."

"Tell me! What does it matter?"

"Old woman, you must never tell anyone! Because I was beaten and starved every day in the temple, I ran away. Look, my hands and feet are all injured."

"Is this true? Then you can't live here, because people from the Dawang Temple often come to our house!"

"Ah!" The child started to cry when he heard this. "Old woman, what can I do!"

"There's no way. You try to imagine our kind of family, how can we bear such a big disaster! You should go to the east street, there is an old lady there, she is very kind and might take you in!" The old woman said to the child with great compassion.

The wind blew harder and harder, and the rain fell harder and harder. In the wind and rain, the old woman watched the child's staggering back as he walked away.

The Barbaric Actions of Civilized People 232

— An

Recently, another case of an American sailor beating a Chinese person to death has occurred in this city. From a humanitarian point of view, this is an extremely unfair matter. It has often been heard that foreigners beat Chinese people without cause within Chinese territory. It is not known why this particular incident happened again. However, now that someone has been beaten to death again, it is only natural for the Chinese people to express their dissatisfaction. It is hoped that this will not be seen as some kind of anti-foreign action.

As one of the Chinese people, I cannot help but be stirred with some emotion when our unfortunate compatriot is brutally killed by an American sailor. However, my indignation does not exaggerate and accuse this as the behavior of foreign imperialist countries bullying the Chinese nation. I am dissatisfied with those who always claim to be civilized people and like to call others barbarians! If others are barbarians, then they are undoubtedly civilized. Here, I want to ask: Is beating people for no reason civilized or barbaric? If the answer is civilized, then the meaning of civilization is a bit vague. If it is barbaric, then this kind of barbaric action is often performed by civilized people. From this point of view, civilized people who are used to calling others barbarians are themselves barbaric.

Is wantonly committing violence the reason why civilized people are civilized?

Companions in Picking Cloddy Rice Roots 233

— Qing Feng

At that time, my family was neither rich nor truly poor; it wasn't as if they were waiting for me to gather grass to burn for cooking, but it also couldn't be said that it was purely for recreation. Partly due to my mother's encouragement, and partly due to my own curiosity, I carried a manure basket and a small grass hoe, and joined the large group of children to pick cloddy rice roots.

It was October.

The large sun, as if covered with dust, had lost its power from the summer days, revealing a gray-red face, quietly watching the ground. The wind in the open fields, because there was nothing to block it, could rush and ram, and seemed even more vigorous. The sky was gray-yellow, the ground was gray-yellow, the tree branches were gray-yellow, and the houses were gray-yellow.

But we weren't sentimental; how could innocent children know these things? We only felt that it was fun to play like this. The wind was our opponent in a race, and perhaps we thought that because our opponent was strong, it made us seem even more heroic?

Those children were all rough children; they were the children of poor farmers, they had grown up struggling through hardship, which could be seen from their ugly but sturdy faces. They hadn't been to school, they didn't understand manners; they used cursing instead of greetings, and fighting instead of affection. Sometimes they fought until they cried, sometimes they fought until their heads were broken and bloody, but they didn't care, it would be fine after a while, and they would still be together. In their group, the only one with a bit of refinement was me, because I was still a child who hadn't left the study yet. They didn't envy me; in their minds, they hadn't yet been instilled with the poisonous "all occupations are lowly, only studying is high". They just looked at me with strange eyes. Perhaps they were wondering:

"Why doesn't this kid curse? Why doesn't he like to fight?"

Although in my own opinion, I felt much wilder than the other children of my station.

We were like a swarm of bees, rushing to the harvested rice root fields. The broken-off root hairs, like a many-fingered hand, tightly grasped the dirt, and the place where they were grasped was taller than other places. We cleverly used grass money to knock on it, first knocking off the large chunks of dirt, then picking it up, scraping it a few more times on the money teeth, throwing away the loose dirt stuck on it, and then putting it in the manure basket, before going to find the second mineral head clod.

Everyone worked hard, fatigue, we can't say there wasn't any, but we forgot. We even competed to see who could pick the most.

Like this, we could pick two manure baskets every day, one in the morning

Page 20

once, and once in the afternoon. When I laboriously carried the manure basket full of cloddy rice roots home, my mother would always greet me with a smile and take the manure basket. Sometimes, if my father was nearby, she would proudly boast:

"My son is gradually becoming useful."

So I was happy, I felt that I had received more than ordinary reward. But what encouraged me to pick cloddy rice roots wasn't just my mother's praise. Because I firmly believed that if I had to do such heavy and laborious work alone at home, I would get tired before I picked two, and no matter what my mother said, I would run away. However, in the open fields with the angry wind howling, in the open fields with the gray sand covering the sky, sometimes with water streaming from my eyes, and sometimes with snot hanging down, I was excited to work. This can't be said to not be because of those small, rough companions.

They were all interesting people, seeing innocence in vulgar curses, and showing nature in vicious fights, with no insidious plots, no cunning tricks, no forced smiles with tears, and no joyful false cries. People like this, today, are like gold in the sand, very difficult to find.

Now, we are far away from each other, the memory's negative is gradually fading in color; and the past events of childhood, only the vague shadows remain. What kind of life are they living? Apart from my imagination: skeleton-like farmers, fierce-looking bandits, beggars wandering the streets, and starving corpses rolling in the ditches?

Yes, what kind of good life can they still live? Since age can take away our innocence, won't fate also deprive us of our happiness?

Beside the Xiangzi Bridge 234

— Jing Fu

"Those days living beside the Xiangzi Bridge can never be forgotten!"

Suddenly drifting back to the traces of the secluded Xiangzi Bridge, I can't help but murmur these thoughts in a daze. However, what can never be forgotten will also be forever impossible to see again. The past beside the Xiangzi Bridge, where have you gone? ...

The more I feel that the days beside the Xiangzi Bridge were extraordinarily beautiful, the more it evokes painful memories, those dreamlike beautiful days that have disappeared and cannot be recovered!

It seems that my numb heart and brain are still under the Han River flowing under the Xiangzi Bridge, impacting the wall under the bridge, and the gurgling splashes are playing an idle and ethereal melody; distant and hazy, the smoky past gently surges up beside the leisurely Xiangzi Bridge...

That was from the age of fourteen, when I was studying at the foot of Han Mountain. I often walked along the secluded embankment, disappearing into the depths of my beautiful and quiet hometown; and from the overlapping mountains, I quietly floated out to the side of the Evil Stream, stepping on the poetic sandy beach, and approached the ferry. The light boat slowly swayed, and looking towards the distance, I crossed under the verdant Jinshan, the clear and broad mood was like water and like a dream, this was an innocent and beautiful heart that had never been beaten by wind and rain! Peeking south from the low awning of the ferry, often at the time when the setting sun was infinitely good, the slanting sun sprinkled on the water surface, like strands fluttering with the ripples of the turquoise crossing, yearning to watch. Unintentionally listening to the clear sound of the ferryman moving the pole, echoing the low sound of the water, all the worries of the world are forgotten. The boat slowly moves forward, as if connecting to the pontoon bridge under Jinshan, one boat after another, piling up and meandering, lined up across the river, and fearfully spreading far to the Jiangbian at the foot of Han Mountain. This is the Xiangzi Bridge! In the rushing Han River, dozens of large stone docks pulled from the Linjiang of Dongmen end, arranged in a straight line, floating pointlessly, spread out to the Han Mountain on the opposite bank across the river, The piers are full of shops, and the bridge is filled with many ancestral halls, all selling snacks and Lingnan's special fruits. There are also countless tourists and travelers scattered around. It is said that this beautiful Han Bridge was built by Han Xiangzi, the immortalized nephew of Wengong.

Our school buildings are located between the foot of Han Mountain and the Xiangzi Bridge, some are on the mountain, relying on the pure and quiet Han Mountain, overlooking the wonderful and lovely Xiangzi Bridge in the clear Han River flowing around the city, studying leisurely as if in a dream, wandering at the foot of the mountain, strolling on the bridge and beside the bridge, what longing days! Quiet and drunk, sitting in the dormitory, the door facing the cool Lingnan wind, floating gently. Silent and infatuated, leaning against the cool pavilion pillar of the campus outside the dormitory window, silently watching the flowers and listening to the songs of cicadas, holding a painting, a young man's mood is a beautiful dreamlike scene! When the weather gets hotter, take a bath in the gurgling mountain pits to your heart's content, listen to the birds singing, listen to the low melody of nature, or leap into the Han River to swim. The spring breeze blows warm, strolling on the secluded mountain, as if sleeping sweetly. When night comes, the moonlight leaks like silver through the seams of the leaves, and shadows scatter under the trees. Or drag to the Xiangzi Bridge, climb the bridge and look around, as if watching a wonderful painting, poetic and lush. Three or five friends, not smiling at each other, chanting poems in a low voice, shouting boldly, breaking through the beautiful night, draped in thin clothes, dragging wooden clogs, leaning against the bridge railing to listen to the sound of water, chewing lychees, and chewing cage rounds. Looking back at Han Mountain, the secluded and lofty school buildings shrouded in silver mist are smiling quietly. Walk down to the sand boat in the middle of the river and watch the countless lights of the boatmen twinkling, and the clear and leisurely songs of the Hakka women on the boat. The turquoise waves beside the sand boat are slightly wrinkled, and I am still unwilling to go home late at night!

However, where are the scenery beside the Xiangzi Bridge? How can anyone not be saddened by the memory of this beautiful dream of the past few years of life rolling in blood? What is there to chase after the old dream! There is nothing to chase after, the Xiangzi Bridge may be dilapidated today, but there, my soul is deeply imprinted!

New Hope 235

Amateur Mailbox

Discussion on Early vs. Late Marriage 236

——A General Response to Readers——

Recently, the editor has received many letters from readers, all inquiring about and discussing the issue of early versus late marriage. Some advocate late marriage, saying that early marriage has many harms; others advocate early marriage, also presenting many examples. However, they are somewhat doubtful about their own views and dare not say definitively that they are correct. Therefore, they write to propose their views and discuss them with us, requesting a clear indication.

Regarding the issue of early versus late marriage, I believe it is very important. Now, I will briefly describe my views below as a general response, and I will no longer reply to individual letters. I hope readers who inquire about this issue will pay attention.

The perpetual maintenance of human life relies on the reproduction of the two sexes, and marriage is the means to achieve reproduction. Therefore, marriage is not only a personal issue but also an important task in human development. If we do not study all aspects of marriage and blindly marry, the consequences will affect the future of humanity.

Under the old ethics, marriage only focused on false and impractical etiquette. As for the physical development of the two sexes and whether the age of marriage was appropriate, little consideration was given. Generally, parents, influenced by the ancient saying "When a son is grown, he should marry; when a daughter is grown, she should be wed," and wanting to experience the joy of having grandchildren, quickly arranged their children's marriages to fulfill a lifelong wish. As a result, many people encountered adverse outcomes due to marrying too early.

When a person reaches around fourteen years old, although it can be as early as twelve or as late as seventeen, special changes occur in the body. This change is a symbol of sexual maturity, medically called the "onset of puberty." During this period of puberty, both the body and mind of the two sexes undergo special changes. In particular, they feel the need for sex, and the previously vague distinction between the two sexes becomes clearly recognized.

Since the need for sex begins at the onset of puberty, the earliness or lateness of puberty is, of course, greatly related to the age of marriage. Therefore, the age of marriage in various countries is determined based on the earliness or lateness of puberty. Generally, people in temperate zones experience puberty earlier, and early marriage is more common; people in cold zones experience puberty later, and early marriage is less common.

Many people advocate holding marriages at the beginning of puberty. Their reasons are:

(1) Sexual desire is a human instinct. Marrying when one knows the need for sex is unlikely to cause any harm.

(2) Early marriage can eliminate harmful masturbation and nocturnal emission.

(3) Early marriage can prevent immoral behavior and avoid the danger of venereal disease transmission.

These reasons do have considerable merit and cannot be absolutely denied. However, we should know that although sexual development is mature during puberty, the development of other parts of the body is not yet complete. If marriage is based solely on sexual maturity, regardless of other circumstances, it will inevitably have the following consequences:

(1) It will affect the health and development of the body.

(2) The children born will be physically unsound due to congenital deficiencies, affecting the development of the race.

(3) Underage men and women have weak wills and are often unable to restrain excessive sexual desire.

(4) They are too young and lack sufficient knowledge to serve as role models for their children.

Early marriage not only has these drawbacks, but even from an economic and intellectual point of view, marrying too early will never yield good results. While we oppose early marriage, we also do not advocate marrying too late, as each has equivalent harms. Based on various circumstances, we believe that the best age for men to marry is twenty-five or twenty-six, and for women, twenty-one or twenty-two. As for masturbation and venereal disease, they are indeed harmful and undesirable behaviors, but they can be remedied through "sex education." Under the old ethics, parents believed that discussing sexual desire with others, especially their children, was a dirty and despicable act. This view is, in fact, wrong. Many scholars in foreign countries advocate that children aged ten to thirteen should be taught simple knowledge of the anatomy and physiology of the reproductive organs; around the ages of thirteen to sixteen, they should be told about the harms of masturbation and the dangers of venereal disease. As for all seductive books, lewd pictures, and obscene plays, they should be strictly prohibited from children. At the same time, efforts should be made to arouse children's interest in studying and vigorously promote children's sports, so that the elements that constitute sexual energy are consumed in the pursuit of learning and physical exercise. Allowing sexual instinct to be naturally restrained is indeed a good method.

Unfortunately, education in our country is not yet widespread, and there are too many stubborn parents. Who can break the false ethics and promote sex education?

Opening Chapter "Daughter"

Apricot flowers bloom in the second month. The daughter of a high-ranking family is as beautiful as a fairy. Naturally beautiful and charming. In her eighteenth year of youth. Cherry lips. Classical Prose 239

Wang Bingmei's Donglai Bo Yi

Huaxing (1260) 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Marquis Min of Jin and Quwo

The distinction between嫡 (dí, of the main wife's lineage) and 庶 (shù, of a concubine's lineage), and between elder and younger, is what Heaven has created, not what humans have done. The sages established fixed rules. Those who have a state should pass it on to the eldest son of the main wife. Those who are sons of concubines should all know that their position comes from Heaven, not from humans. Since the beginning of civilization, everyone has followed this rule and dared not change it. It is not only because they fear the sages, but also because they fear Heaven. Therefore, Wei Zi dared not replace Zhou, Mu Yi dared not replace Duke Xiang, Zi Xi dared not replace King Zhao, and Ji Zha dared not replace Zhufan. With the virtue of these wise men, if they had inherited the throne, they could have expanded the achievements of their predecessors and laid a foundation for endless prosperity. However, they hesitated and declined. Is it not because they could not bear to sacrifice the interests of millions of generations for the sake of one person's private desires and create a disaster of endless strife? The distinction between嫡 (dí, of the main wife's lineage) and 庶 (shù, of a concubine's lineage), and between elder and younger, is what ancient and modern sages dared not lightly change. Who was Marquis Min of Jin? He dared to be the first to create chaos. Drowning in private love, he recklessly made light or heavy distinctions when naming his sons, leading to the disaster of Quwo and ultimately destroying the state. Yet the Zhou kings favored him.

Supplement of Shen Bao 本埠, Movie Special

Ziegfeld’s Idea of Ugly Became Stars in the Film Industry (Part 2) 241

— Xin Ni

As for facial features, Ziegfeld's so-called beauty is even more different from the currently popular Hollywood beauty. There may be some actresses there whose two eyes are exactly the distance of another eye, or whose pupils are exactly the same distance from the tip of their nose to their eyebrows -- these are a few points of the beauty standard, but who cares so much about it. Hollywood beauty cannot be measured by regular circles and squares.

Constance Bennett is considered beautiful in Hollywood, but her square chin and small nose not only do not meet Ziegfeld's standards, but also may not be considered beautiful by ordinary people, but she is considered a beauty on the screen. Take Joan Crawford, her pair of large nostrils are completely out of proportion to the rest of her nose, and her forehead is completely masculine, but she is still a beauty on the screen.

Many other actresses have special defects in their faces. Like Ruth Chatterton, her mouth is obviously large and useless. Anne Harding's face has two halves that are different from each other. Clara Bow's face is concave on the top and convex on the bottom. In terms of expression, the beautiful Norma Shearer's face is half indifferent and half enthusiastic. Jean Harlow's nose has an abnormal angle.

In short, most of the beauties in Hollywood, such as Fay Wray, Gloria Swanson, Helen Hayes, Winne Gibson, Nancy Carroll, Ruth Chatterton, Lupe Velez, Dolores del Rio, Claudette Colbert, and Katharine Hepburn, etc., would be considered failures according to Ziegfeld's standards.

Breaking Ziegfeld's standards and being able to become stars in the film industry is not limited to the above-mentioned actors who have long been famous. Even Mona Loa, who has recently become very popular, does not meet Ziegfeld's standards. Her appearance is completely boyish, and she is full of freckles, and she is not a good-looking boy, but no one can say that she is ugly. As for the other newcomers, such as Elizabeth Begner from England, and the child stars who have risen, such as Qin Muya, Jean Parker, Josephine Hutchinson, etc., almost none of them meet Ziegfeld's standards.

It is true that very few of the current Hollywood actresses meet the standard of Ziegfeld's beauty, but on the other hand, if the chorus girls under Ziegfeld were put in Hollywood, I am afraid that none of them would have any hope of success. This is not only because of the changes of the times and different perspectives, but also because what the naked eye calls beauty may not look good in front of the camera. Darryl Zanuck, the head of United Artists, once said: "Since the prevalence of sound films, no actress has been able to become a star solely on the beauty of her face. The beauty of the face in the photography field is only worth eight dollars a day; but the brain can be worth one hundred dollars a day; if the face and the brain are combined, then it can be worth one thousand dollars a day!"

A beautiful mind... this is the Hollywood way. Therefore, a Ziegfeld beauty must have exceptional intelligence to hope to become famous in Hollywood. Maureen O'Sullivan is a very prominent example. Others, such as Ruby Keeler, Jean Blondell, and Noel Francis, have also been members of Ziegfeld's beauty team, but they all feel that jumping from the song and dance world to the film world is no longer a shortcut to success, and a beautiful face is no longer the password to Hollywood. (End)

Exploration of Film Education and Film Bookification 242

— Bo Ning

On Wednesday evening, the school showed educational films. The night self-study class was stopped, but the fruit stalls at the gate were still surrounded by a large group of students. In the dark self-study room, someone was pulling a Jinghu, brightening his throat to sing "Wujiapo." I wondered, "They don't want to pay to see a show, what is the reason?" I grabbed a younger classmate and asked him. He curled his lips and disdainfully said, "Who wants to see it? They always show things like papermaking, fishing, and planting pearls. You'll get tired of watching it half the time." So, a "?" was immediately added to my mind.

I think the reason why movies can attract such a large audience is because their interests are multifaceted. They are based on various human instincts to create various plots. Humans have the instinct for "sex," so there are a large number of love movies. Humans have the instinct for "fighting," so there are many war movies. Humans are "curious," so a whole batch of detective movies appear. Humans like to "seek knowledge," so many animal movies and various news movies are born. In short, humans have several instincts, and movies have several natures. They are constantly changing and adjusting, so the general audience also enjoys them and never gets tired of watching them.

Now, educational films extract a part of the movie and only focus on the aspect of human pursuit of knowledge. The materials they take are either history or geography, either production undertakings or pioneering undertakings, and they do not consider that human instincts are multifaceted. Therefore, although the intention is good, it is a pity that it is too rigid, too unvaried, and does not fit the psychology of the audience, so it becomes a moving textbook, and it is no wonder that young people shake their heads when they see it.

In fact, if we want to achieve the effect of film education, we must not abandon the current advantages of film, and we should make full use of them. We still need love movies, detective movies, and war movies, which are closely in line with people's instincts. However, when making them, we should take into account the educational value in terms of material selection, structure, and performance, so that the mission of film education will not be difficult to complete. If we insist on extracting a part of the movie and calling it "educational movie," then in a few days there will be "industrial movie," "commercial movie," and "agricultural movie," and the result will be one moving textbook after another.

The Magnificent Scenery in "The Beginning of Man" 243

The Yihua Company is serious about the "scenery" in the film, and is unwilling to be perfunctory, which has already been proven by facts. "Escape" cost tens of thousands of gold, and went to Mongolia, Suiyuan, and Chahar to take real location shots. In "Woman," more than 5,000 yuan was spent to build a building, which was then burned down... These are all sacrifices that other companies are unwilling to make. Now, the sound film "The Beginning of Man," directed by Mr. Shi Shushan, also has very magnificent scenery, and the scenery of Suzhou streets, small rivers, wharves, etc., that was shot in the past two days is even more magnificent, because these sceneries were all taken by the scenery artist Mr. Fang Peilin in Suzhou in advance with a camera, and the scenery built upon returning was built according to everything in the photos. For example, the boats in Suzhou are different from those in Shanghai, so two boats were specially rented from Suzhou and moved to the Suzhou River excavated by the company. Although many people think that Yihua's sacrifice is "stupid," in fact, only such "stupid work" can obtain beautiful results. Hollywood film companies mostly do such "stupid work" for scenery, so Yihua Company has the style of Hollywood.

Meiqi Evans and Wu Liefu's performance in "The Rest of a Piece of Meat" - Nanjing Ying

In the day when film companies are urgently feeling the need to cultivate new talents and create child stars, Zhaohua Company's move is especially worthy of our deep attention! (Que)

Amateur Reporter (After Office Hours) (6) 246

— Tongyun

After James Bolton walked away, Dennis Bader took Sharon's hand and said, "Don't be angry that I came out with them. Julia insisted on dragging me along. I couldn't embarrass her too much. But their constant bickering is unbearable, and I can't spend too much time with them. I'm afraid it will interfere with the most important thing in the world to me..." His voice lowered as he trailed off. At that moment, Julia came chasing after them. She said to Sharon, "Ha, Sharon, why don't you come sit with us? Come on... you and I... have a lot in common... for example, we can both talk about Tommy..." Sharon said softly, "Julia, I think you should go back. Henry is coming." Julia had no choice but to return dejectedly. As she left, she turned back and called out, "Tommy, come back soon."

As soon as Julia left, Dennis Bader said to Sharon, "Let's not sit here. Let's get a motorboat and go play at my place." Sharon immediately agreed. So they went out together. By the time James finished his phone call and returned, Sharon was nowhere to be found.

Soon, Dennis Bader had taken Sharon to his villa. It was a very exquisite stone house built on a hillside on the north shore. Behind it was a small mountain with extremely serene scenery. There was also a boathouse by the water, connected to the outer waterway. Many nosy people often speculated about how Tommy Dennis Bader had gotten this house and how he maintained it. He was originally completely penniless, but since the bank collapsed, he was even worse off than before, completely broke. They arrived there and went inside. Sharon took off her coat. Dennis Bader took Sharon's coat and lowered his head to kiss her fragrant shoulder. He lit the kerosene lamp and sat with Sharon on a low sofa. He held her hand tightly and said softly, "My heart, I don't know how much love it can hold." Sharon patted his hand, not saying a word, but her eyes were full of amorous feelings, as if she couldn't contain herself. After a while, she said, "Tommy, I always think you should stay away from the Patterson's. She's simply crazy about you. Of course, it's very difficult for you. If you weren't such a gentleman, you probably would have ignored her long ago..." Suddenly, there was the sound of a motor on the river outside. Dennis Bader's ears were sharp, and he heard it, but Sharon was lying on the sofa, her eyes half-open and half-closed, very comfortable, and she didn't hear it. Dennis Bader stood up and said, "I'll go get some wood. Let's make a fire to keep warm." His expression looked very flustered, but Sharon didn't see it. She just turned slightly and said, "No need to make a fire. It's too late, we'll be leaving soon." Dennis Bader deliberately acted coquettishly and said, "Let's make a small fire, as a souvenir. When I see the fire here alone in the future, I will think of tonight."

As he spoke, he went out to get wood. Before he left, he put a record on the gramophone, and the room was immediately filled with music. It turned out that Dennis Bader went outside and a motorboat docked in front of his house. Sure enough, as he had expected, the person in the boat was Julia Patterson. Julia jumped ashore and said fiercely to Dennis Bader, "I know Sharon Trot is here. I want to reason with her, and tell her what you are to me. I really can't take it anymore." Dennis Bader blocked her path and grabbed her clothes, which were made of thin silk, and immediately tore. (To be continued)

Shen Bao Local Supplement Automobile Weekly

Psychological Requirements for Car Drivers 247

— Bo Ning

Cars. Many people give it the terrible nickname "City Tiger". Because every day. Every week. Every month. Car accident cases are continuously discovered. People who lose their lives under cars continue to increase. No wonder ordinary people fear them.

However. The car itself is improving day by day. Transportation facilities are also being actively improved. What is the remaining problem? It is people. It is the selection of drivers. From a psychological point of view. Drivers must at least avoid the following negative shortcomings.

(1) He is not colorblind. People who are colorblind. Often cannot distinguish various colors. Even the mildest red-green colorblindness. They also cannot distinguish red and green. We know that the signals currently used in traffic. Are mostly red and green lights. If a driver cannot distinguish red and green. Will he rush around and be able to follow traffic rules? Distinguishing whether a person is colorblind or red-green colorblind is very simple. Just use several colors to let him distinguish them.

(2) He does not have astigmatism. People with astigmatism. Their eyes are often easily tired. Vision can never be focused. And hallucinations often occur in front of them. If a driver. His vision cannot be focused. He often has hallucinations in front of him. Isn't that a very dangerous thing. If you want to test whether a person has astigmatism. It is very easy. Just give him a picture with lines to test it. If he can clearly see the lines next to him. He does not have astigmatism. If he looks at it and some lines are clear. Some lines are blurred. Then he is unreliable.

(3) He does not have motor incoordination. People with motor incoordination. Often cannot control their own movements. Usually his movements are normal. Sometimes suddenly his hands and feet will be confused and disordered. Imagine a person driving a car. Driving on a busy street. Suddenly there is motor incoordination. That is dangerous enough. To test whether a person has motor incoordination. It is also very easy. Just blindfold his eyes. Call him to stand with his two toes together. If he stands very steadily. Then there is no problem. If his body cannot support him. And seems to be about to fall. Then he is unreliable.

(4) He does not suffer from automatic reactions. People who suffer from automatic reactions. Can be said to be the most dangerous. If he is driving a car on the road. He sees another car. Driving very fast. He will chase after it involuntarily. Many car accidents are due to this aspect. It is difficult to check people with this kind of problem. Only observe his daily behavior. See if he is quiet and steady. Because people with this disease. Mostly cannot sit quietly for an hour or two.

The above four psychological defects. The obstruction to drivers is very serious. People who have not learned to drive. Should first measure whether they have such shortcomings. To avoid learning in vain, and those who have already learned. Should also measure themselves. If you find such defects. Would rather give up this career. So as not to waste energy. But have bad consequences. As for the municipal authorities that examine car drivers. And those who employ drivers. They should pay more attention to the above four conditions.

New Overview of Williams 248

— Yun

Sedans, coupes and panel delivery trucks. Are the three new styles of Williams for 1935. The headlights of Williams. Originally a whole part of the wing panels. Now it has been moved. Even closer to the water tank. Redesigned engine hood. Inclined water tank grid screen. Lowered wing lines. The car body is made entirely of steel. Total length is 155 inches. Main bearings. Made of hard metal. Pistons are made of cast steel. Equipped with three compression rings and one oil deflection ring. Fully floating on the piston pin. All models of cars. Unified installation of movable front seats. The car body is insulated. Not affected by the climate. And can isolate sound. The gasoline pool is completely hidden. Inverted carburetor. Larger air purifier and silencer. Pressure lubrication. Double drop × type frame. Hydraulic shock absorbers. Steel driving board. Steel core safety steering wheel. Four wheel plug car. Single piece clutch and transmission. It is popular. The glass installed on the front and rear windows. When lowered. That is beyond the line of sight. In addition to all the above. This year's new Williams car. Can also be equipped with a specially constructed folding luggage compartment. Its accommodation location. Up to eight and a half square feet or more.

Manufacturing situation of the new Packard car 250

The factory of the new No. 120 Packard car. Can be called the most modern and practical in the automobile industry. The sophistication of manufacturing car bodies and chassis. It can also be said to be perfect. Most of the machinery manufacturers in various parts of the United States. Mostly recruited by him. To engage in installation engineering. For almost a year. The precision and efficiency of the machinery in the car. Is actually a new record in the machinery industry

Mechanical experts from all parts of the United States have come to the Packard Company's factory. To study the engineering of installing new cars. They said that the new method adopted by the One Hundred and Twenty Packard cars. Will definitely be imitated by the public in the future. The result can make the machine gradually improve.

Packard Company has divided its largest factory into two parts due to the manufacture of new cars. One factory specializes in manufacturing twelve Packard and eight Packard. Another factory specializes in making one hundred and twenty Packard. Each factory has its own independent mechanical department. To manufacture various metal accessories on vehicles. There are also assembly departments and car body manufacturing plants.

The factory of the One Hundred and Twenty Packard car is extremely spacious. Divided into three floors. The first floor is a whole big room. About four acres or more. Includes machinery department. Assembly department and testing department. The two floors above are the car body department. The machinery and methods used in it are the latest. Can break all previous records in the automobile industry. Therefore, the superiority of the One Hundred and Twenty Packard car. It is really beyond the reach of other cars.

Reaching 7,000 units per day

Michigan, Di Di Bang News. Ford Motor Company has been introducing 8V engines for three years. Production is increasing day by day. According to the company's Diabang headquarters. The domestic production volume stipulated in the past. The biggest should be in March of this year. Its planned production is 160,000 vehicles.

According to the March plan. The company will build 7,000 vehicles per day. In order to supply the increasing demand for 1935 Ford V8 passenger and freight vehicles from outside inquiries. Production in March this year. Compared with the production of 77,947 vehicles in March last year. It will more than double.

Summary of New US Traffic Regulations in 1935 255

— Zhenmin

The new regulations for driving cars recently promulgated by the US government's car administration office. Its strict restrictions. The thoroughness of consideration. Xun was unprecedented. Now I extract several important points. As a reference for road administration agencies in our country

(1) Speed ​​limit: The maximum operating rate of cars on lit thoroughfares must not exceed 30 miles per hour. Driving on dim roads. Must not exceed 20 miles per hour. Those who violate the regulations for the first time. Punishable by a fine of twenty gold pounds. A repeat offender. The fine reaches fifty gold pounds or more.

(2) Driving test: Those who have passed the driving test and obtained a notice on September 1, 1934. May be exempted from being tested again. Later comers must undergo rigorous testing. If there are still dangerous and careless driving incidents after passing the test. Then you must undergo a second test. Those who fail the retest. May not obtain a notice. However, those who fail the retest may submit another request to the authorities for a retest.

(3) Dangerous driving: Anyone who violates the dangerous driving regulations (such as speeding, etc.) is subject to imprisonment for six months for minor offenses. Serious offenses range from one to two years.

(4) Careless driving: Those who violate this regulation. Suspend his driving rights for one month. Repeat offenders are suspended for three months.

(5) Vehicle inspection: The structure and all accessories of the vehicle. Must be inspected by the car office. All vehicles that do not meet the conditions stipulated by the car office. Generally speaking, driving is not allowed. Purchase, manufacture, transfer or reservation.

(6) Compensation for vehicle injury: Each injured person is certified by a doctor. You can ask the car owner to compensate 12 shillings and six pence for medical expenses. The cost of calling a doctor. Calculated at six pence per mile. It is also borne by the car owner.

(7) Death from being run over: The driver or car owner can be accused of dangerous driving. At the same time, the prescribed pension is paid to the family members of the deceased. (Preset by a car office)

Since the promulgation of this law. Its obvious effect. It is a sharp reduction in the number of car accidents. According to statistics in January. The number of accidents decreased by 35% compared with the average monthly number in 1934. From this, the perfection of the new law can be seen.

Statistics of Car Sales by American Manufacturers and Top Ten Cars in 1934 256

— Shadow

—Ford First, Chevrolet Second—

What was the business situation of American automobile factories in 1934? Regarding the statistics of total car sales for the whole year, we have not yet received a confirmed report. However, the sales statistics of each factory from January to September 1934, for the nine months, have already been published. Moreover, during these nine months, the increase or decrease in the sales records of each factory has largely determined the situation for the whole year. Therefore, we will first translate the confirmed number of new car registrations of each factory in the United States during these nine months to inform the readers of this publication.

Page 28

Before we talk about the total number of cars sold by each factory in the nine months, we should first mention the car sales records of each factory in September. In September, American automobile factories in Detroit produced a total of 146,931 cars, which is 7% lower than in September 1933, and 24.2% lower than in August of the same year. However, in terms of the total number of cars sold in the nine months, a total of 1,564,690 cars were sold, which is still an increase of 29.9% compared to the same nine-month period in 1933.

In September, Chevrolet surpassed Ford in the number of cars sold and won the first place, with a difference of about 1,000 cars. The total number of Chevrolets was 43,003, accounting for 29.3% of the total, while Ford had 41,929 cars, accounting for 28.5% of the total. Third place was Plymouth, with a total of 24,551 cars. According to the statistics from the new car registration offices in various provinces, Chevrolet ranked first in 32 states across the United States, while Ford ranked first in 16 states. In Colombia, Ford also took the lead, while Plymouth ranked third in all provinces, but in Colombia, it surpassed Chevrolet to take second place, exceeding Chevrolet by 36 cars, and was also very close to Ford. These three leading vehicles accounted for 74.5% of the number of registrations in various places in September, which was slightly higher in August. Individually speaking, the order of the top ten cars did not change in September compared to August.

Oldsmobile had 1,500 more cars than Dodge and won fourth place. Pontiac surpassed Buick by 131 cars and took sixth place. Studebaker was 100 cars less than Studebaker, ranking ninth, while Chrysler originally ranked tenth. Although the total number of Oldsmobiles ranked fourth, Dodge ranked fourth in as many as 21 states in terms of provincial distribution, while Oldsmobile only had 19 states. In addition, Pontiac also competed with it, accounting for fourth place in two states. Others, such as Buick accounting for four states and Studebaker accounting for one state, all won fourth place.

In terms of the total number for the nine months of 1934, Ford still ranked first, with registrations increasing by 211,579 cars compared to 1933, which was the same as the general expectations of the automotive industry beforehand. The three low-priced cars, Ford, Chevrolet, and Plymouth, had the strongest sales. Chevrolet's registrations increased by 39,449 cars compared to the previous year, and Plymouth by 61,923 cars. The total increase for the three companies was 312,923 cars compared to the previous year. In terms of percentage statistics, some vehicles increased even more than the above three. For example, Hudson's registrations for nine months totaled 15,851 cars, while in the same period in 1933, it was only 2,534 cars, an increase of 525.5%. Studebaker increased by 11.8%. The combined number of Nash and Lafayette increased by 119% compared to Nash alone last year. Although Lafayette was a new vehicle last year, its registrations in September were also as high as twelfth. Others, such as Studebaker, increased by 165% in nine months compared to last year, Oldsmobile increased by 96%, LaSalle increased by 38.1%, Cadillac increased by 18.4%, Graham increased by 27%, Buick increased by 27.4%, Ford's percentage increased by 89.1%, Chevrolet by 10%, and Plymouth by 32.1%.

The following table lists the ratio of American car registrations from January to September in the past two years. The order is based on the first letter of the car name in English.

Sichuan Province Works Hard to Build Roads 258

— (New News Agency)

Chairman Chiang Commends the Chengdu-Chongqing Road Project, Guo Shu-gao Assists Tang Shi-zun's Planning

Chongqing Communication. Liu Xiang, Chairman of the Sichuan Provincial Government, has been working hard on road construction in recent years. However, due to the geographical conditions of the province, the road construction work has been quite difficult, especially in the Laoyingyan section. Fortunately, Tang Shizun, the Director-General of the Sichuan Provincial Highway Bureau, upholds Chairman Liu's intentions and embodies Chairman Chiang's spirit of hard work. He has supervised his subordinates and is determined to proceed. Moreover, Guo Shufu, the former special envoy of the road, has assisted Tang with all his strength, which is quite remarkable. This time, Chairman Chiang visited to give instructions on the suppression of bandits and showed concern for road administration. He personally inspected the Laoyingyan section of the Chengdu-Chongqing Road and saw that the project was huge and the design was well-considered. He praised it as the top project among the national highways. Director-General Tang is a great construction talent and deeply admired Tang's spirit of taking on important responsibilities. In addition to first sending Director He to announce the commendation, he also immediately sent a telegram of praise to commend him. In addition, the completion of the five major highways of Sichuan-Hankou, Sichuan-Guizhou, Sichuan-Gansu, Sichuan-Shaanxi, and Sichuan-Hubei is truly urgent. Therefore, he specially telegraphed the Sichuan Provincial Government, the two road bureaus, and the relevant provinces to expedite the construction so that they can be completed as soon as possible. In terms of funding, Chiang has agreed to first subsidize 1.2 million yuan from the central government to start construction in order to ease the burden on the people of Sichuan.
